Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek's Reflections After Arriving in Chongqing

Speech at the Expanded Memorial Week in Chongqing

(Chongqing) Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek attended the expanded memorial week for party, government, and military personnel on the morning of the 11th and gave a speech. He briefly stated that since his arrival in Chongqing, nearly ten days ago, he has observed the local social and political aspects and is pleased with the generally good situation. Today, he will offer a few points based on his observations. First, if we want to improve society, complete the revolution, and build a modern nation, we must first ensure that all citizens of the country, especially the staff of party, government, and military institutions, possess the basic common sense that modern citizens must have. The reason why China is in such a state of national crisis and popular suffering is generally believed to be the lack of military strength for self-defense. However, this is only a superficial and secondary reason. The fundamental and important reason is that the general public, and even those in the party, government, and military who are responsible for governing the country and leading the people, lack the common sense of modern citizens. Therefore, striving to enrich subordinates and the general public with this kind of common sense is the most crucial and fundamental urgent task for us in revolutionary nation-building from now on. The so-called common sense of modern citizens has many aspects, which cannot all be described in detail. The most important thing is to recognize that the nation is an organic organization, just like an individual with life, spirit, will, and appearance. The national flag is the sacred appearance of the nation, and the national anthem is the solemn sound of the nation. Therefore, wherever the national flag and national anthem are, we know where the nation is. All citizens, no matter when or where, must unanimously respect and cherish them. Moreover, the national flag must be made in accordance with regulations, be neat and uniform, be hung with respect, and be raised and lowered on time, so that people will be respectful when they see it. When singing the national anthem, one must be dignified, have a measured tone, and a harmonious voice, so that people will be solemn when they hear it. Because to make the people's minds consistent and their spirits united, we must first pay attention to the national flag and national anthem that they see and hear. Therefore, seeking uniformity in the size of the national flag and the intonation of the national anthem is the most important and basic common sense for uniting the spirit, unifying the will, and cultivating modern citizens. Second, the general malady of Chinese people today and the reason why all undertakings cannot be promoted lies in following old ways and being content with the current situation, being perfunctory and irresponsible, being half-hearted in doing good, and being unheroic in doing what is right. If we want to correct these current ills and complete the great cause of revolutionary nation-building, our comrades in the party, government, and military must adhere to the spirit of acting bravely upon seeing what is right and being pragmatic, and strive hard according to the two major principles of speed and certainty. That is what I mean by revolutionary nation-building: we must act quickly, practically, and resolutely to succeed. Taking Sichuan as an example, at present, such things as the improvement of police administration, the opening up of roads, and the speedy resolution of lawsuits are all the most urgent and essential tasks for seeking governance. However, we must pay special attention to time and cherish time. We must know that all undertakings are born of time. Wasting time or delaying time is tantamount to cutting off our own path to survival. In short, everyone who knows and can act must persevere to the end. As for how to adapt to local conditions and adapt to the times to increase the effectiveness and promote perfection, it is also something that those in power should consider. Third, the key to governance and construction lies in being good at organization, training, management, rewards, and punishments. When used properly, we should always use the labor of the local people to open up local transportation, cultivate local land, and increase local production. We must know that the labor of the people is the basic quantity for nation-building, and it is also the driving force of funding. If we can only organize and use it, we will be able to complete various construction undertakings to seek economic prosperity and bring the country to the realm of wealth and strength. Moreover, in this time of national distress and popular poverty, only by making poor plans and first carrying out construction undertakings that do not cost money can we have the possibility of completing the revolutionary construction. In the past, places like Jiangxi and Hunan have worked hard in this way and have achieved great results. Sichuan has always been known as the Land of Abundance. If it can catch up quickly, its success will be far-reaching. However, the people of Sichuan have been in distress for a long time, and their strength is exhausted. Therefore, the organization and use must not only be appropriate, but nurturing the morale of the people, protecting the strength of the people, and cherishing the lives of the people are the sole and most important tasks of those responsible in the party, government, and military. Today, the people of Sichuan stand on tiptoe and their shapes are disappearing, their faces are full of smoke, and this is the case everywhere. This is truly the deep pain of the nation and the shame of comrades in the party, government, and military. From now on, how to cultivate the morale of the people, protect the strength of the people, cherish the lives of the people, and organize the masses and use the labor of the masses is our greatest responsibility and the only great cause of revolutionary construction. The above points are all based on my recent observations. I hereby sincerely offer them, and I hope that our comrades in the party, government, and military, under the leadership of Chairman Liu, will jointly and consistently implement them in accordance with the principles I have presented today. If we do so, the completion of the construction of a new Sichuan can be expected soon, and the foundation for the revival of the nation will be laid here. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 12th)

The Yellow River in Southern Hebei Continues to Rise Sharply, Hebei Provincial Government Schedules Meeting, River Bureau Chief Requests Emergency Measures, Changyuan County Establishes City Defense Committee

(Tianjin) Because the Yellow River in southern Hebei has risen sharply, and the efforts to block the flood have failed, creating an extremely dangerous situation, the Hebei Provincial Government has specifically scheduled a meeting at the Yellow River Disaster Relief Association on the 15th to decide on flood prevention and relief measures. Hua Deming, director of the Hebei Yellow River Affairs Bureau, telegraphed the province, stating that the Yellow River is still rising continuously, the flow is rolling north even more severely, the labor and materials are exhausted, there is no land to take soil from, and the sacks are all used up. He is requesting instructions on emergency measures. (Special dispatch on the 12th)

(Tianjin) The relocation of Changyuan County has already identified two locations east of the river, Lugang and Chuntingji. They are awaiting the arrival of Commissioner Ye Zhenmin from the province to survey and determine the location. Changyuan County has established a City Defense Committee, with gentry and civilians serving as members. They have gathered 3,000 laborers to block the entire city and rescue the people. They plan to build an arc-shaped dam outside the east gate, six li long, divided into four sections. The county magistrate of Changyuan telegraphed that the Taihang Dike has been affected by the rising water of the Guantai River, and the water level has increased, already two feet from the dike surface. The dike is in extreme danger, collapsing as quickly as it is blocked. He is requesting a large sum of money to raise the dike three feet and widen it eight feet to prevent it from collapsing. (Special dispatch on the 12th)

International Loans to China, Britain Makes No Proposal, Lord Privy Seal Makes Statement in the House of Commons, Says Only Urged Powers to Pay Attention to Chinese Finance

(London) The British Lord Privy Seal, Anthony Eden, stated in the House of Commons today that the British government has not proposed any international loans to China. Recently, newspapers have repeatedly carried news of international loans, believing that this proposal was initiated by Britain, causing people to have the impression that Britain, the United States, France, and Japan were discussing and proposing loans to China. Last week, British Foreign Secretary Simon stated in the House of Commons in response to a question from Lumley that the British government had no such plan. Today, Eden reiterated this statement, wanting to dispel incorrect impressions. A spokesman for the British Foreign Office stated on March 2 that what Britain had already done was, at China's request, urge the United States, France, and Japan to pay attention to China's financial difficulties. (Reuters dispatch on the 11th)

(New York) Japanese Ambassador Saito gave a speech at a foreign press banquet tonight, stating that the only purpose of Sino-Japanese friendship is the tranquility of East Asia and the gradual reduction of commercial and investment risks, and definitely not to reject Western participation in China's reconstruction. Saito also stated that there is no such thing as low social or labor endowments in Japanese business operations. If rumors can become reality and China no longer boycotts Japanese goods, then obvious commercial barriers can be removed. The world's recession is mostly caused by economic nationalism. Britain and the United States should work hard to eliminate commercial barriers. Japan deeply feels that the freedom of trade is an important prerequisite for the world's recovery. (Reuters dispatch on the 12th)

Current Commentary

Restrictions on Foreign Rice and Adjustment of Rice Supply and Demand

— Ren

On the 7th of this month, the Executive Yuan, at the request of the Shanghai Municipal Government, specially convened a review meeting on restricting the import of foreign rice in the capital, attended by representatives from the Ministries of Finance, Industry, and Interior, the Rural Reconstruction Committee, and the Shanghai Municipal Government, to decide on appropriate measures. After consultation, the opinions of all parties were combined into three points: The first point, the issue of the impact of foreign rice imports on the outflow of cash, has been handed over to the Ministries of Finance and Industry to study together with the case of rescuing industry and commerce. The second point, the issue of whether tariffs should be increased on foreign rice imports, has been decided to be determined based on the circumstances. The third point, the issue of whether full taxes should be levied on broken rice imports (currently half taxes), has been handed over to the Tariff Commission for review and decision.

The import of foreign rice into our country has been increasing in recent years, increasing more than tenfold compared to twenty years ago. Such a large amount of foreign grain being imported is due, on the one hand, to the dumping of surplus goods from overseas. On the other hand, the desolation of our country's rural areas and the frequency of droughts and floods are also the main reasons for promoting the large influx of foreign grain. During the summer and autumn last year, there was a severe drought for several months, and the rice harvest was poor. According to a survey by the Shanghai Rice, Bean, and Miscellaneous Grain Association, excluding the rice-rich areas of Wenzhou and Taizhou in Zhejiang Province, there was a shortage of about 2 million dan. Jiangsu Province had a shortage of 1 million dan. Provinces like Anhui had a slight surplus, while Hubei and Hunan were generally self-sufficient. Jiangxi was able to supply itself. In total, there was a shortage of about 3 million dan in the Yangtze River basin. As a result, grain prices rose sharply in various places, and domestic and foreign rice merchants rushed to purchase foreign grain. According to reports from various foreign firms, as of the end of last year, the number of orders had reached more than 5 million bags, already exceeding the shortage. Since the beginning of this year, rice merchants have been placing orders one after another. It is heard that forward foreign rice for April and May has also been pre-ordered to more than 800,000 or 900,000 bags. If this continues, then the "expensive grain" of last autumn will become the "cheap grain" of this spring. The Chinese farmers who are currently "selling green seedlings" will neither benefit from the "expensive grain" of last autumn nor avoid losses from the "cheap grain" of this spring. The future of the rural areas is full of worries, and the impact on the restoration of China's economic prosperity in the future will inevitably be another obstacle.

The Executive Yuan has convened a meeting at this critical juncture to try to reverse this difficult situation, which is certainly essential. However, the results of this meeting are only to save the current crisis, and it may not be enough to lay the foundation for the future. To prosper China's economy, we must start with revitalizing the rural areas. This is a truth that everyone knows. However, the revitalization of the rural areas should, on the one hand, study how to eliminate the roots that shackle today's rural areas and reduce the burden on farmers. On the other hand, we should study how to increase the income of farmers so that they can have sufficient food and clothing. If we advance on both sides in this way, the rural areas can recover, and industry and commerce can also prosper accordingly.

The main income of farmers is grain. Therefore, if we want to increase the income of farmers, at least the grain price must be in line with the cost of cultivation and must not fluctuate drastically. However, if we want to stabilize the grain price, we cannot but rely on the power of the government, and the government must have a definite and unchangeable policy. In other words, today, in order to revive the rural areas and adjust the people's food supply, the government should quickly and precisely investigate the national consumption of rice and grain, and then formulate certain laws and regulations, ordering rice and grain producers, rice merchants, and rice and grain warehouse operators to report the amount of rice and grain in stock at any time. When necessary, the government should conduct actual inspections to observe the proportion of supply and demand. At the same time, it should also refer to the cost of rice and grain production, general living expenses, and the trend of the rice price index to the price index to determine the highest and lowest prices. If the market price falls below the lowest price and the supply exceeds demand, the government can purchase rice and grain, increase foreign rice taxes, or restrict foreign rice imports to regulate the grain price. Conversely, the government can sell rice and grain, reduce foreign rice taxes, or exempt foreign rice taxes. In this way, the supply and demand of rice and grain can be adjusted, and the grain price will not fluctuate drastically. The benefits to farmers from this will be not small, and its contribution to the revival of the rural areas will certainly be significant. Today's meeting of the Executive Yuan is only temporary in nature, so what is discussed is naturally based on the current facts. If the situation changes in the future and new facts and phenomena occur, then a second meeting must be reopened. If this happens again and again, it will not only be uneconomical in terms of human resources, but it will also not be a "one-stop shop." Therefore, we deeply hope that after this review meeting, the government should seek a proper method to adjust the supply and demand of rice and grain to overcome the current difficulties of the recession.

After the Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway Is Concluded, Japan Takes Further Steps Towards Russia, Seeks to Resolve Various Pending Issues, Starts with Negotiations on Oil Rights First, Border Dispute Negotiations Are Difficult

(Tokyo) The draft agreement for the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway was signed at 9:30 p.m. on the 11th. This negotiation, which began with the first official negotiation on June 26, Showa 8 (1933), has lasted for one year and ten months, with a total of 56 meetings (including 6 official meetings, 24 meetings between Foreign Minister Hirota and Russian Envoy Yurenev, 4 intermediate consultations, 8 meetings between Director Togo of the European-Asian Bureau and Russian Representative Kozlovsky, and 16 drafting committee meetings). It can be seen how difficult the negotiations were. There were repeated crises on the verge of breaking down. However, as a result of Foreign Minister Hirota's efforts to mediate, it was successfully completed. After the signing yesterday, Foreign Minister Hirota and the Russian envoy continued to talk, exchanging various opinions on the fundamental adjustment of Japanese-Russian relations. The Foreign Minister said that the Eastern Railway negotiations had been concluded, and it was a matter of great congratulation for the peace of the Far East and Japan, Russia, and "Manchukuo." Japan and Russia should resolve various pending issues before this friendly atmosphere dissipates, using effective methods, starting with the easy issues and gradually moving into the difficult ones. The Russian envoy replied that his government expressed sympathy for the Foreign Minister's views and hoped that both sides would resolve the pending issues in a spirit of mutual concession. As a result, the two countries first began negotiations on the extension of the pilot mining rights for oil in northern Sakhalin, and gradually discussed the issues of the Border Dispute Mediation Committee and the revision of the Fisheries Treaty. (Japan Associated Press dispatch on the 12th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army Department expressed the following opinion on the conclusion of the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway: Although the Russian-"Manchukuo" dispute over the railway can be eliminated as a result of the sale, if Soviet Russia does not abandon its ambition for the Far East, it will inevitably make greater efforts to consolidate its borders. Therefore, unless Soviet Russia has sincerity, the conclusion of this negotiation will not have much effect on the easing of Japanese-Russian relations. (China United Press dispatch on the 12th)

Contents of the Russian Puppet Protocol

(Moscow) TASS learned from the authorities that the documents for the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway were signed today, including the Soviet-"Manchukuo" contract, the Soviet-Japanese-"Manchukuo" triangular protocol, and various official documents that must be exchanged between the Soviet and Japanese governments regarding the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway.

The main points of the Soviet-"Manchukuo" contract are as follows: The preamble states that the purpose of this contract is to promote peace in the Far East and stipulates that the "Manchukuo" government shall pay 140 million yen (excluding the Soviet employees' retirement fund of about 30 million yen). The Soviet Union will transfer all its rights to the Chinese Eastern Railway to "Manchukuo." One-third of this amount, 46.67 million yen, must be paid in cash. Of this, 23.33 million yen must be paid as soon as the contract is signed. The remaining half will be repaid by the "Manchukuo" Ministry of Finance in four installments over three years, each installment being of equal amount, with an annual interest rate of 3%. The contract stipulates the so-called "gold reservation item," that is, if the exchange rate of the yen continues to fall, the amount received by the Soviet Union must also be increased proportionally. The remaining two-thirds of the total amount, 93.33 million yen, will be paid by Japanese-"Manchukuo" commercial institutions according to the Soviet trade delegation's orders in Japan within three years. The price of these goods is stipulated to be paid by the "Manchukuo" Embassy in Japan through the Bank of Japan. After formally signing this contract, "Manchukuo" will be the owner and operator of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The contract also stipulates the procedures for the transfer of the railway's assets and liabilities.

Another part of the contract stipulates the protection of the Soviet employees of the railway, that is, all Soviet employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway who are dismissed by the new Manchukuo administration can receive their full salary in accordance with the current regulations of the Chinese Eastern Railway. They can also resolve all their financial issues with the railway, receive subsidies, and so on. The contract also stipulates that there shall be no mutual disputes over property rights between the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Soviet Railway. At the same time, an agreement is specially concluded to resolve the passenger and freight traffic between the Soviet and Manchukuo railways. The clauses listed in the Soviet-Japanese-"Manchukuo" triangular protocol stipulate that the Soviet trade delegation must order goods from Japanese-"Manchukuo" merchants under normal conditions. If there are any disputes between the Soviet trade delegation and Japanese-"Manchukuo" merchants, a special mediation committee will be established to resolve them. The committee will have four members, including two representatives from the Soviet Union and one each from Japan and Manchukuo.

When signing the contract, the Japanese government must hand over to the Soviet Embassy a document guaranteeing the cash and goods to be paid to the Soviet Union for the Soviet Union's abandonment of its rights to the Chinese Eastern Railway. The Japanese government will also use a document to guarantee that all payments must be made to the Soviet Union. The contract will take effect from the date of formal signing. (TASS dispatch on the 11th)

Statistics on the Entire Property of the Eastern Railway

Since February 27, the Eastern Railway Creditor's Rights Committee, with Li Shaogeng, the superintendent of the Chinese Eastern Railway, as its chairman, has reviewed the results of the report on the creditors' and debtors' rights of the Eastern Railway submitted by the director of the administration, and has learned the full picture of the Eastern Railway's property, which was previously unclear. According to the committee's calculation, the total amount of creditors' rights is 106,376,328 rubles, and the total amount of debts is 16,525,010 rubles. The main creditors' rights are as follows: (1) Cash and deposit amount: 4,739,892 rubles; (2) Reimbursement of government organs of "Manchukuo" and troop transportation fees: 57,829,480 rubles; (3) Troop transportation fees for the Japanese army (September 1934): 16,394,588 rubles; (4) Joint military debt (September 1, 1934): 14,071,831 rubles. The main contents of the debts are as follows: (1) Salaries of staff, allowances for retirees, and other unpaid accounts: 1,524,103 rubles; (2) Unpaid expenses for workers and organs: 587,249 rubles; (3) Debts to the Chinese customs and other government organs of "Manchukuo": 36,240 rubles. (Japan Associated Press dispatch on the 12th)

Disposition of the Shanghai Property Is About to Happen

It is learned that the East China Railway Wharf at Yangjiadu in Shanghai covers an area of about 20 Chinese acres and is located between the Japanese Mitsui & Co. wharf and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's West Wharf. There are also warehouses and the real estate of the railway's Shanghai office on Sichuan Road, which are also worth more than one million yuan. According to the agreement signed this time, all rights to the Eastern Railway's various affiliated enterprises and properties will be transferred to the management of the puppet organization, and the South Manchuria Railway will inherit the Eastern Railway's operating rights. Therefore, it has been decided to accept the Yangjiadu wharf and the office building on Sichuan Road in this port. The authorities of the office recently registered the wharf's real estate with the US consulate in this port. The transfer of the wharf and real estate may cause problems. (News Agency)

Japan's Economic Status Becomes More Consolidated

(Electric Communication News dispatch on the 12th)

Full Text of Illegal Agreement on the Eastern Railway

News Agency reports that the Soviet Union illegally sold the Chinese Eastern Railway. The draft agreement was signed at 9 PM on the 11th. This matter is currently undergoing formal negotiations from our side to Russia. How the outcome of future negotiations will proceed remains uncertain. The full text of the draft agreement is now obtained as follows:

(1) Items to be sold: the Chinese Eastern Railway and all its affiliated assets. (1) (A) The railway's total length is 1,726 kilometers, being the trunk line between Manchouli, Suifenhe, and Changchun. (B) 2,544 kilometers are for business lines, 2,567 kilometers for telephone water supply equipment and telegraph lines. (1) All locomotives and freight cars owned by the railway. (1) Various factories, forestry rights, and all properties belonging to the railway. (2) Sale price: 140 million yuan, and approximately 30 million yuan for Soviet staff severance pay. (3) Terms of sale: The price of 140 million yuan is to be paid in cash and goods. One-third of the price is to be paid in cash, and two-thirds in goods. The time limit for both is three years. (4) Method of cash payment: Half of the amount is to be paid immediately after signing the agreement, and the remaining half is to be paid in six installments within the three-year period, with annual interest at a rate of three percent. Payment will be in Japanese yen. If the price of the Japanese yen against the Swiss franc fluctuates by more than eight-tenths, the exchange rate of the Japanese yen will be changed according to the current price. (5) Method of payment in goods: After the agreement is signed, the purchase price will be offset by goods needed by the Soviet Union, such as rice, raw silk, silk fabrics, small ships, electrical machinery and appliances, fishing nets, copper tea, and soybeans produced in Japan and Manchukuo. However, the Soviet Union does not want weapons. The price of the goods will be determined by a review committee composed of two members from the Soviet Union, one from Japan, and one from Manchukuo. If there are difficulties, Japanese goods will be handled by the Soviet-Japanese governments, and Manchukuo goods will be handled by the Soviet-Manchukuo governments. (6) Guarantee of Payment: The Japanese government will issue a written notice to the Soviet government, stating that it guarantees that Manchukuo will pay all cash and goods within the limited period. (7) Railway handover and connection with other lines: (1) In order to clearly understand the assets to be handed over, a balance sheet should be prepared in Harbin in the near future as a standard. (1) The properties owned by the Soviet Union are the Soviet Consulate General, staff dormitories, library, hospital, and school. 1. Regarding the connection between the Ussuri and Siberian lines, the Chinese Eastern Railway will connect at the Manchouli and Suifenhe stations. Rules regarding connections will be agreed upon separately after the purchase and sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway is officially established. (8) Period of takeover: After signing the agreement, all rights will be officially taken over at the same time. (9) Dismissal severance pay and allowances for Soviet staff: A. When dismissing Soviet railway staff, notice must be given three months in advance. After the notice, Soviet staff members will return to their country, and will be given a grace period with the right to free transportation on the Chinese Eastern Railway. C. In addition to severance pay, savings should be paid immediately upon signing. As for allowances, they are limited to be paid off within two years.

New York Cotton Market Plunge

Due to Misunderstanding of Bankhead Amendment Government Control Plan Still Uncertain

(New York) The New York cotton market was extremely panicked today under the great pressure of selling, causing the price of cotton per bale to plummet by more than five dollars. The stock market was affected by this, with prices falling by two dollars. The Chicago wheat market was also affected, with prices falling by two cents. The reason for the cotton market's instability is that the government's plan to control new cotton production is still uncertain. The government decided that farmers producing less than two bales of cotton would not be subject to the Bankhead Cotton Acreage Control Act. This move also shook the cotton market's confidence, as it could render the control plan ineffective. All parties were dumping large quantities of cotton into the market. Senator Bankhead stated that the amendment to the Cotton Acreage Control Act could not increase the total amount of new cotton production to more than ten million five hundred thousand bales. He supports stockpiling five million bales and not selling them on the market. After this statement was made, the price drop temporarily subsided, but the market situation was still not stable. (Reuters, 11th)

(Washington) Senate Agriculture Committee Chairman Smith stated today that, in view of the sharp drop in New York cotton market prices, he will urge the House to prepone that the government stockpile at least five million five hundred thousand bales of cotton until prices rise and export trade recovers, and then may sell. He argues that the cotton stockpiled by the government should not be used for offsetting debts, nor should it be sold before December 1, 1936. If necessary, he will advocate stockpiling more than five million five hundred thousand bales, as this is a practical objective that Congress can control. People in the cotton industry should now know that Congress definitely intends to accomplish this. Bureau of Agriculture Director Davis IV stated that the policy of the cotton farmers' public accumulation agency has not interfered with the market, and the government has no intention of abandoning the cotton field loan program. Officials are not paying much attention to today's cotton market price drop, believing that even if farmers are now selling cotton, the amount is very small, so farmers are not greatly affected. The reason for this price drop is due to the misunderstanding of the Bankhead Cotton Amendment by people in the cotton industry. The amendment advocates that farmers producing less than two bales of cotton should be exempt from taxes, while the government's March regulations only apply to landlords. Whether this type of amendment can pass is still questionable. (Reuters, 11th)

British House of Commons Great Debate Expansion of National Defense Plan Baldwin Defends with Eloquent Words Labor Party Impeachment Motion Defeated by Majority Many Women Distribute Pro-Peace Leaflets

(London) The Labor Party's motion to impeach the government, opposing the government's policy of expanding military strength, resulting in an increase of ten million fifty-three thousand nine hundred pounds in this year's net expenditure, was rejected by a majority in the House of Commons tonight. The Labor Party only received seventy-nine votes, while those opposing the motion numbered four hundred and twenty-four. This debate, which has attracted international attention, had many spectators, and many nobles were seated in the special viewing gallery, listening attentively. The French, Belgian, Turkish ambassadors, and the German embassy counselor were also among them. During the heat of the debate, an unexpected interjection occurred. Many women threw leaflets advocating peace from the viewing gallery. Pieces of paper flew around, scattering throughout the venue. These people also loudly criticized the White Paper on National Defense, and were immediately escorted out by the parliamentary police. Soon after, several more women in the viewing gallery performed the same antics and were also expelled. At the same time, two hundred people, mostly women, gathered in the outer room of the parliament, intending to see the members of parliament in order to oppose the government's policy. Fortunately, security was tight, and no incident occurred. Amidst the sound of debate, there were also noises of contention. Labor Party member Attlee moved to impeach the government, stating that the White Paper denies the League of Nations, destroys the League of Nations' fundamental principles, making it impossible for the League of Nations to be effective, and also that the White Paper is causing an arms race, frightening the world. When the mover spoke, government party members shouted "Nonsense!" in response. The subject of debate was a military expenditure budget estimate, which differed from those previously proposed by members, and this budget estimate was being discussed for the first time, so tonight's debate was particularly noteworthy.

Labor Party Impeachment Denounced as Nonsense

The impeachment motion asks the House of Commons to express its opinion on whether the government's national defense policy is completely contrary to (1) the spirit of establishing collective world peace by creating the League of Nations, (2) hindering the atmosphere for the establishment of an arms reduction convention, (3) leading to international competition and insecurity, and brewing war. Attlee claimed that when Foreign Secretary Simon was preparing to have friendly talks with Germany, the government unexpectedly published the White Paper on National Defense, angering Germany, which was regrettable. The government seems to have never supported other countries' arms reduction plans. The Labor Party always detests any form of military action, domestic or otherwise. The White Paper clearly indicates a complete change in Britain, returning to the atmosphere of alliances against enemies and the arms race in the skies before the European War. Government party members loudly denounced it as "nonsense."

Baldwin on the Status of the League of Nations

Privy Council President Baldwin stood up to reply, speaking very movingly, saying that the democratic government has stated in the White Paper what it considers to be the truth of democracy. In the past, there have often been major crises unfavorable to democracy because the leaders of democratic governments did not reveal truths that people did not want to hear. It is not true that the British government has only paid lip service to the League of Nations. Since the establishment of the League of Nations, any statesman of any political party in Britain has always done their best to support the League of Nations at all times under very difficult circumstances and against the opposition of countries that have already withdrawn from the organization. The British government is still determined to work for the future in the League of Nations, but people are prone to forget when talking about collective security and sanctions that the membership of the League of Nations is not universal, so the collective system is not complete. Two major countries have now announced their withdrawal, dealing a major blow to the collective system. In addition, there is another major country that has never assumed the obligations of the League of Nations. The British government earnestly hopes for the universalization of the League of Nations, and for this reason, welcomes the Soviet Union's joining the League of Nations, and has always strived to persuade Germany to withdraw its withdrawal notice. It must be known that in international politics, one does not do what is ideally the best, but what is best in the existing environment. The government is not now proposing to expand its military strength, but merely proceeding with the air force expansion that was debated last summer. What it is requesting is that once all its forces must resist an aggressor or fulfill obligations under the convention, it should be as well-equipped as possible.

White Paper Not Aimed at Germany

Baldwin mentioned the joint communiqué issued after the British-French talks in London, saying that the direct and effective cooperation with Germany mentioned in the communiqué is of particular importance in the view of the British and French governments, hence the arrangement for Simon to visit Berlin. The visit to Berlin should be realized in about half a month. Each party has its own desires in this kind of event. There are countries that wish to amend existing treaties, and there are countries that are asked to agree to these amendments. No one can blame the former if they wish to slightly change the status quo, but what can be reasonably requested is that the changes they desire should be accompanied by the safeguards necessary for peace and security. Some parties believe that the White Paper is only aimed at Germany, which is not true. However, what the White Paper says is essentially the same as the remarks he made last November with general agreement. These remarks, made in a friendly spirit and with genuine understanding, are the best and only effective prelude to any negotiation, and the trust that, without candor and genuineness, the beginning of an effective agreement is impossible, let alone the ending. He hopes that the government can now handle things seriously.

Franco-Italian Negotiations Open a New Era

If the negotiations that have already begun in Paris and Rome continue to be conducted in other capitals, there is no reason to say that they cannot create a new era for Europe. The British government is watching the continuation of these negotiations and is prepared to make contributions, but the desire to create or expand false matters, or the effort to grasp the facts, will not be of any benefit.

Replenishing Armaments Only Seeking Equality

Baldwin responded to the claim that Britain's national defense plan would lead to other countries rearming, and pointed out the facts and figures of the already greatly increased military strength of other countries such as the United States, Japan, and Russia, saying that the United States has now built warships to the limits permitted by the treaty, while Britain has not yet done so. The US naval budget has increased from 350,000,000 yuan in 1933 to 492,000,000 yuan in 1935, and the increase in 1936 is even greater, reaching 580,000,000 yuan. From these figures, it can be seen that even under the constraints of the treaty, Britain now feels that its military strength has not enabled Britain to achieve equality. Baldwin went on to mention the Franco-Italian navies, saying that while other countries are building various weapons at an alarming rate, Britain has not increased its army or navy. If a new agreement on warships cannot be established, the replenishment of British warships will soon become a critical issue. British warships need the latest equipment and protection against aircraft in many ways, which the United States and Japan are already rapidly doing. The British army is not fully prepared for large-scale military operations, and the British air force still ranks fifth among the world's air forces. Even today, Britain does not want to compete with the largest air force, but only wants to maintain its equal status with strong countries that are slightly closer in distance.

Air Force Convention Aims to Ensure Security

Many of today's disappointments arise from the issue of status. Britain must pay attention to this matter in future discussions. Many countries are now adopting the major plan of mobilizing the entire nation once war breaks out. Britain has never been a leader in rearmament. All of Britain's air force still ranks fifth. In addition to defense equipment against aircraft, it has not increased its army or navy strength. Britain cannot guarantee itself against air strikes, but can make air strikes more difficult. This is the aim of the air convention that has been submitted. In any case, air strikes must be made worthless anywhere in Europe. The policy stated in the White Paper is not only harmless to peace, but can also make future peace more secure. We must all hope that our representatives who will travel to the capitals of Europe in the next two or three weeks will work smoothly, and that the security we are striving for will be realized soon.

Simon Continued to End the Debate

Samuel, a leader of a portion of the Liberal Party, claimed that the British government is now beginning an arms race, and that competition will have no end except for bankruptcy and war. Foreign Secretary Simon rose to end the debate, saying that he stated with the full agreement of the government that British policy is entirely based on membership of the League of Nations. Britain does not want to restore the methods that existed before the collective system was established. The most important aim of the current negotiations is to seek conditions under which Germany can rejoin the League of Nations. We firmly believe that there is no world guarantee that can rival the effective work of a genuine and universal League of Nations. Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain then put forward his amended answer, which read: "The House of Commons is loyal to Britain's obligations as a member of the League, and is willing to limit armaments through international compromise, while acknowledging that this goal cannot be achieved through unilateral disarmament. It now approves the government's policy, recognizing that there is an equal need to protect the people and fulfill international obligations.

Clearly Respond to Aggressor Nations

The former Foreign Secretary said that the League of Nations can certainly provide great protection against occasional wars, but there is no guarantee against the aggression of countries that deliberately wage war to achieve their ambitions. To prevent this kind of war, the only way is to clearly indicate to this aggressor nation that it will be met with overwhelming force, so that it cannot have any hope of victory. The Locarno Treaty, the Eastern European Pact, and other local agreements all take this as their policy, and have become effective methods for consolidating the collective system.

Glimpse of the Contents of the White Paper

As for the content of the White Paper, the responsibility of the House of Commons is to announce to the people of the country that the sacrifices required by the White Paper are necessary for Britain's national defense and the fulfillment of its obligations as a member of the League of Nations. The important figures in Britain's defense budget estimate are as follows: the Air Force will increase by forty-one and a half squadrons by the end of 1938, with an increase in expenditure of £3,089,000, totaling £20,650,000.

The Army will increase by 2,700 men, totaling 152,200 men, with an increase in expenditure of £3,950,000 over the previous year, totaling £43,500,000.

Naval expenditure will increase by £3,500,000 over the previous year, totaling £60,050,000, with an increase of 2,000 personnel. The warship construction program includes three cruisers, one leader ship, eight destroyers, three submarines, one submarine supply ship, four supply ships, one survey ship, and seven small warships. (Reuters, 12th)

Greek Civil Strife Suppressed Rebel Leaders Flee to Italy and Bulgaria Order Gradually Restored in Various Places

Athens Prime Minister Tsaldaris recently declared to the press, "After the rebels in northern Macedonia and Thrace were eliminated, government agencies have all been restored to their posts. The rebels have fled in droves, taking away the contents of local treasuries." (Havas, 12th)

Athens This afternoon, government forces captured Kavala, Drama, and Thessaloniki. All three places are strategically important. The rebels, having lost them, will have no way to resist. It is expected that they will completely collapse within seventy-two hours. Rebel leaders such as General Kamenos have fled to safe places. According to a Reuters report from Sofia, General Kamenos led seventy-two staff officers and crossed the border into Bulgaria this afternoon, taking refuge south of Mastanli. Macedonia and Serres are now declared clear. The rebels on land have been bombed by aircraft and have already surrendered. The authorities now believe that the rebel ships will also surrender within a few days. Government forces marched in and occupied Serres. General Kaminos, seeing that his troops had no will to fight, fled to Alexandroupolis with several staff officers. Upon hearing that the area had also surrendered, he hurriedly turned back. Government officials in various cities in Macedonia and Serres have resumed normal administration. The government has ordered that the rebel leaders captured in the battle will be tried by military tribunals. Prime Minister Tsaldaris told a Reuters interviewer today that once the rebellion is suppressed, a new era for Greece will begin. According to a Reuters report from San Remo, General Plastiras, the mastermind of this rebellion, attempted to cross the border into Italy near Bordighera in Italy today, but was stopped by the Italian authorities and returned to Genoa. It is reported that before abandoning Serres, the rebels looted the local Greek bank, taking away 80 million Greek coins. Before attacking Serres, government forces heavily bombed it with artillery, and then advanced through the snow. After a brief but intense battle, the rebels were defeated. The enemy's morale was greatly reduced, thousands surrendered, and hundreds fled into Bulgaria. (Reuters, 11th)

Rebel Leaders Flee Venizelos Arrives on Italian Island

Sofia The rebel commander Kammena, who commanded the fighting in the Macedonian sector, and eighteen officers and the Governor of Serres Province retreated into the Bulgarian border this afternoon, where they were disarmed by the Bulgarian border guards. The commander said that the entire army was defeated due to a mutiny of the soldiers. It is reported that the chief of staff of the rebel Fourth Army Corps has committed suicide. Government forces Commander-in-Chief Kontylis, seeing that the fighting in the Macedonian sector has come to an end, will return to Athens by plane tomorrow morning. (National News Agency, 12th)

Athens According to unconfirmed but reliable sources, former Prime Minister Venizelos, Naval Admiral Dimitrios, former Finance Minister Maris, and many other rebel leaders have boarded the Averoff cruiser and left Crete with their followers. It is also reported that after escorting the rebel leaders to a safe location, the ship will return and be at the disposal of the government. Crete Governor Apotsokidis, who had been detained by the rebels, has now been released and has restored all civil servants to their original positions. (National News Agency, 12th)

Athens Mr. and Mrs. Venizelos and sixty officers are reported to have landed in Dutenes, Kasos Island, Italy, today. His ship then sailed back to Greece, preparing to surrender to the government. Mr. Venizelos is seventy-one years old this year and is the "father of the nation" of the Republic of Greece, having unified the country and expanded its territory, but he still cannot avoid fleeing to other countries. The government has not yet announced what action it will take against Mrs. Venizelos, who is wealthy, but said that it has been discovered that Mrs. Venizelos has funded the revolution and purchased weapons for the rebels. (National News Agency, 12th)

Athens The government has recently requested the Bulgarian government to extradite the rebel officers. According to news from the Tetovo district, a battalion of rebels planned to escape by train, but was disarmed. In addition, Serres rebel commander Brigadier General Ranatopoulos, along with five staff officers, escaped in a sailboat equipped with a motor and disappeared without a trace. Minister of Cabinet Metaxas replied to journalists that if a foreign country intervenes to mediate the unrest, the Greek government considers it an unfriendly act. All countries agree with the Greek government's view that there should be no intervention. (Havas, 12th)

European Air Force Convention Goering Indicates Willingness to Participate Simon to Decide Trip to Germany in Geneva

(Berlin) The local newspapers all published extensively Prussian Governor Goering's remarks to Daily Mail reporter Old Bleitz, and paid particular attention to Goering's statement that while the German Air Force will defend the motherland and will not retreat even a single soldier, it will never threaten the peace of other countries. As for the British-French invitation for Germany to participate in the Air Force Convention, Goering expressed that Germany is happy to accept it in order to jointly maintain peace. Goering also explained the distinction between Germany's military and civilian aviation, saying that it can be known from the different badges of aviation personnel. However, Germany's military aviation is directly under the jurisdiction of the Minister of Aviation. Although Goering's words did not explicitly state the strength of the German Air Force, the world should generally recognize that Germany must have an air force to protect the entire country, which is undoubtedly the intention. (National News Agency, 12th)

(London) Privy Council President Baldwin stated in the House of Commons today that Foreign Secretary Simon's planned trip to Berlin has been delayed, but it is expected to take place within two weeks. (Reuters, 11th)

(London) The Daily Mail diplomatic correspondent cabled that the date of British Foreign Secretary Simon's visit to Berlin can be decided within one or two days. According to diplomatic sources, the British Foreign Secretary hopes to travel between March 24 and 30, so his trip may take place before Lord Privy Seal Eden goes to Moscow. (National News Agency, 12th)

(London) The Times published an editorial today, saying that if the British-German talks are delayed for so long, or even break down, it will allow those who advocate a detached policy to gain a victory, and will cause irreparable damage to Europe's collective security. As seen by The Times, the current situation is approaching a critical point, because giving Germany equal treatment is a generally agreed strategy, and it is imperative. Since the British government has recognized this, it should be clear that the restrictions on Germany's military strength in the Treaty of Versailles have become a thing of the past. Therefore, for the present, it should look to the future as soon as possible, and no longer be afraid of past discrimination. (National News Agency, 11th)

Soviet Russia's Note to Britain: Welcoming Eden to Moscow

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian Foreign Ministry today sent a note to the British government, welcoming the Lord Privy Seal, Eden, to Moscow for Anglo-Russian negotiations. It is understood that Eden will soon come to Moscow to negotiate Soviet Russia's participation in the non-aggression pact for the air force and the disarmament convention recently proposed by Britain. Observers say that the British side intends to persuade Soviet Russia to reduce its Western military strength to dispel Germany's fears, because Hitler insists on revitalizing armaments because he believes that the increasing strength of the Soviet Russian army and air force is sufficient to threaten Germany. If Eden can accomplish his mission and make Soviet Russia agree to disarmament, then Germany should be able to make corresponding concessions, so that Britain and France can also reduce their army and air force. If so, European peace can be expected, and the people's taxes can also be reduced. (Twelfth National Telegram)

Severe Internal Turmoil in Cuba: Capital Announces State of War, Law of Shooting Imprisoned Resurrected, U.S. Maintains Non-Interference Stance

Havana. The cabinet officially announced a state of war. Cuba has become a world of terror today. The barbaric law of killing prisoners, which has long been abolished, has also been resurrected, that is, releasing the prisoners, ordering them to run quickly, and then shooting them from behind. It is understood that six people were executed by the government army in this way last night. The entire national economic undertaking has been completely halted. President Madi Tate ordered, under the dictatorship of Chag, that all people accused of being related to strikes and riots should be tried by military law, and the right to be tried by ordinary courts should be abolished. The national strike wave has reached its peak. Armed troops coming and going in the streets have further heightened the arrogance of the strike. Military officers ordered soldiers not to be lenient to strikers, and if there is resistance, they can be killed without mercy. However, although the laws are strict, the throwing of bombs has not stopped. The law of shooting prisoners has also failed to arouse the people's fear. Observers believe that this kind of action will only make the revolutionary movement more enthusiastic. (Eleventh National Telegram)

(Washington) The State Department announced that the United States does not intend to interfere in the turmoil in Cuba, because it has not received any reports of danger to the lives and property of American expatriates. The State Department spokesman said that if there is no danger to the lives of American expatriates, the internal turmoil of the Republic of Cuba has nothing to do with the United States, because the Platt Amendment has recently been abolished. However, the government is paying close attention to the situation in Cuba. It is said that the diplomatic representative stationed in Havana must report by telegram almost every hour. (Eleventh National Telegram)

Chen Gongbo Discusses the Issue of Aiding Industries

(Nanjing) Chen Gongbo said that the requests from all sectors of Shanghai for assistance to the market, regarding lending and economic aspects, are currently being planned by the Ministry of Finance and Kong Xiangxi. The Ministry of Industry is devoted to studying fundamental solutions. There are many reasons for the decline of Chinese industry and commerce. What is currently manifested is economic hardship and excessive trade deficits. Although there are many relief measures, they will definitely not be achieved overnight. The Ministry deeply feels that to start relief, it must explore the root cause, so it has decided to first conduct a detailed investigation of the names and quantities of imported foreign goods and exported domestic goods, and analyze one by one the points that should be improved in the export of domestic goods. This work is being investigated by the International Trade Bureau on the one hand, and the Ministry is coordinating the entire improvement plan on the other hand. As for the plan to aid industry and commerce, the Ministry will first start from prosperous industrial and commercial areas and plan relief through industrial and commercial cooperation as a fundamental plan. Chen laughed at the external rumors that the Ministry of Industry advocated implementing control over the relief of industry and commerce, saying that the name of control is very new, but unfortunately the general production and sales situation has not yet been clarified, and the nascent industry and commerce of China are not yet at that point. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

National Government Promulgates Revised Fortress and Fortified Zone Law

(Nanjing) The National Government issued an order on the 12th, revising the Fortress and Fortified Zone Law for promulgation. The order, with attached text, is as follows:

Revised Fortress and Fortified Zone Law

Chapter 1, General Provisions, Article 1: The area around various fortresses and fortifications established for national defense is called the fortress and fortified zone. Article 2: The extent of the fortress and fortified zone is based on the various strongholds of the fortress and fortification, and the stipulated distance from the outer edge of this point is included. Article 3: Unless otherwise specified, the fortress and fortified zone, whether land or water, is divided into two zones, as stipulated below: (1) The area from the outer edge of the base point to about 400 to 600 meters in front is the first zone; (2) The area from the boundary line of the first zone to about 3,000 to 4,000 meters in front is the second zone. The above-mentioned zones shall be determined by the Ministry of Military Affairs in consultation with the General Staff Headquarters, but the areas related to military ports, naval ports, and naval defense structures shall be determined in consultation with the Ministry of the Navy and shall be announced jointly. Chapter 2, Restrictions and Prohibitions, Article 4: Restrictions and prohibitions in the first zone (1) Without special orders from the highest military authority, no surveying, photography, drawing, writing, or other military reconnaissance activities shall be carried out. (2) Without the permission of the fortress commander, no fishing, hunting, algae harvesting, mooring of ships, or excavation of sand, soil, and minerals shall be carried out. (3) Without the permission of the fortress commander, no new or altered buildings, piles, tombs, kilns, gardens, walls, ditches, ponds, wells, or engineering projects that change the ground level shall be built. (4) Buildings should be mainly made of combustible materials. If they are built of non-combustible materials, the height should not exceed one meter. (5) The height of piles should not exceed two meters for non-combustible materials and four meters for combustible materials. Article 5: Restrictions and prohibitions in the second zone (1) Without the permission of the fortress commander, no surveying, photography, drawing, writing, or other activities shall be carried out. (1) Without the permission of the fortress commander, no new or altered buildings exceeding six meters in height made of combustible materials, or engineering projects that change the ground level by more than one meter shall be built. However, for parts of buildings made of reinforced concrete, the height shall not exceed one meter without the permission of the fortress commander. (3) Without the permission of the fortress commander, the height of piles should not exceed three meters for non-combustible materials and six meters for combustible materials. Article 6: Matters that should be restricted and prohibited in both the first and second zones (1) Without the permission of the government, foreign merchant ships and warships shall not pass through or moor. (2) Without the permission of the Minister of Military Affairs, no new or altered projects such as railways, roads, canals, bridges, dams, tunnels, and permanent docks shall be carried out. (3) Without the permission of the fortress commander, aircraft shall not fly in the air. (4) The fortress commander may order those residing in or passing through the area who are suspected of spying on military affairs to leave immediately or be escorted out of the area. Chapter 3, Penalties, Article 7: Those who violate the prohibitions and restrictions stipulated in this code, regardless of newly built, altered, reconstructed, or expanded houses, warehouses, and other buildings, or piles, etc., shall be ordered within a time limit to dismantle them themselves. If the terrain is changed, they shall be ordered to restore it to its original state. If they cannot completely remove them or restore them to their original state within the time limit, or if the method they use is not suitable, the official agency may execute it directly or order a third party to execute it, and the expenses shall be borne by the violator. Article 8: Those who violate the prohibitions in Article 4, Paragraph 1, or Article 6, Paragraph 3, shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of one year or less, detention, or a fine of 100 yuan or less. Article 9: Those who violate the prohibitions in Article 4, other than Paragraph 1, or Article 5, shall be sentenced to detention for 15 days or less, or a fine of 5 yuan or less. Article 10: Those who violate the prohibitions in Article 6, Paragraph 1 or Paragraph 2, shall be sentenced to a fine of 100 yuan or less. Article 11: Those who privately move or damage various signs set up within the fortress and fortified zone shall be sentenced to detention or a fine of 40 yuan or less. If it is due to negligence, they shall be sentenced to a fine of 3 yuan or less. Chapter 4, Supplementary Provisions, Article 12: The provisions of this law may also be announced and applied to areas where the construction of fortresses and fortifications has been decided but not yet constructed. Article 13: The Minister of Military Affairs may, at his discretion, lift or suspend all or part of the prohibitions and restrictions of this law in a certain area, but shall announce it in advance, and the same shall apply in case of changes in the future. Article 14: In wartime, the fortress commander may, as necessary according to the situation, order the removal of buildings, piles, and planted items in the fortress zone. Article 15: The fortresses and fortifications to which this law applies shall be determined by order of the Minister of Military Affairs in consultation with the General Staff Headquarters or the Ministry of the Navy. Article 16: This law shall come into effect on the date of promulgation. (Twelfth Central News Agency Telegram)

British Ambassador Arrives in Beijing from Ping

(Nanjing) British Ambassador Sir Frederick Maze, accompanied by counselors and secretaries, arrived in Pu by train from Ping at 8:30 PM on the 12th. British Consul White-Bonney and others stationed in Beijing welcomed him at the station. After the British Ambassador got off the train, he crossed the river with the welcoming personnel, entered the city by car, and went to the Embassy in Beijing to rest. According to the British Ambassador's words to reporters at the station, this visit to pay respects to your country's diplomatic authorities is an ordinary visit and has no special mission. He will stay in Beijing for about three or four weeks and plans to go to Shanghai to handle private affairs. National Government Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting, and Statistics Compiles a Report on the Movement of Silver in Shanghai

(Nanjing) In order to better understand the situation of silver in recent years, the National Government Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting, and Statistics has specially compiled a report on the movement of silver in Shanghai based on the monthly reports on the inflow and outflow of silver from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance. The report provides detailed statistics on the value of silver inflows and outflows over the six years from 1929 to 1934, especially the large amount of silver exports last year. In addition to a table comparing the value of silver inflows and outflows, the report also includes separate figures for the amount of silver that entered and left through the Jianghai Customs and the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways over the years. The book has been compiled and printed and distributed to various places for reference. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Resolutions of the Jiangsu Provincial Government

(Zhenjiang) The Provincial Government resolved on the 12th: 1. To allow the Songjiang Advanced Applied Chemistry Vocational School to purchase the land of the Wang family to the east in accordance with the Land Acquisition Law for the construction of a factory. 2. To approve the resignation of Yang Binru, the Director of the Nanhui Education Bureau, and appoint Chen Guobao as his successor. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Shandong Department Heads Inspect Qufu

(Jinan) The heads of the Civil Affairs and Education Departments inspected Qufu today and met with Duke Yansheng, Kong Decheng, promising to investigate the rent resistance of the Sihe River sacrificial fields. They also inspected Sihe and returned to Jinan tonight. Kong Decheng said that he is currently studying the Five Classics and learning science and English. He has not yet decided whether to study in Beijing. He will definitely not go to Japan. He has refused all visits from Japanese people. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Many Shops in Bian Close Down

(Kaifeng) More than 50 shops in Bian have closed down in the past two months. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Doihara Passes Through Xiamen Without Stopping

(Xiamen) Doihara returned from Guangzhou and went straight to Fuzhou from Hong Kong, without stopping in Xiamen. It was originally scheduled to arrive in Xiamen on the 12th to visit Chiang Ting-wen, but Chiang Kai-shek extended his return to Zhangzhou in Shanghai, so Doihara also cancelled his visit to Xiamen. The Guangdong Maru passed through Xiamen on the 12th and went to the province, and it is said that he took it there. However, the Japanese Consulate did not announce Doihara's whereabouts, saying that it had not received a report of his arrival in Xiamen. It is also said that after Doihara arrives in the province, he will transfer to Taiwan and return to Japan on the 15th or 17th. (Twelfth Special Telegram)

Hebei Provincial Government Resolves to Block the Yellow River Breach

Yellow River Water Rises, Previous Efforts Wasted, Changyuan County Seat Imminent Submergence

Tianjin dispatch: Since the dismantling of the Yellow River Aftermath Project Office in southern Hebei last year, the Yellow River breach closure project has been the responsibility of Hua Deming, Director of the Yellow River Affairs Bureau, assisted by Zhang Qinglu, the magistrate of Changyuan County, to carry out the Guantaigou breach closure project. After eight months, the project has not yet been completed. There was news last month that the Changyuan breach would be closed, but recently, the Yellow River's main current shifted north, scouring the embankment, and the breach reopened, widening to over 45 meters. The Jinmen area is overflowing with water, the current is turbulent, the Taihang embankment is being severely eroded and is also in danger. The water level at the breach has gradually risen from 18 meters. As of today, due to the current slowing in the morning and accelerating at night, the difference in depth between morning and evening is several meters. The east dam is 21.3 meters deep in the morning and rises to 24.5 meters in the evening. The west dam is 20.7 meters deep in the morning and rises to 22.6 meters in the evening. The sides of the embankments are collapsing and being washed away by the current. The ropes used for binding are being battered by the huge waves, breaking nineteen times. In the middle of the night, the ropes snap with a sound like thunder. River officials and Changyuan County officials have supervised six to seven hundred laborers, employees, and soldiers, working day and night to protect the area, but everything they block is washed away. It is found that the Guantaigou project, which was already more than halfway complete, has now been completely wasted. The Changyuan County seat has been surrounded by water for eighteen months. Only one main street in the city remains unflooded. Now, due to the rising water, the water outside the city is 18 meters deep, and inside the city it is about 8 meters deep. Only half a brick of the city wall remains visible above the water. People rely on boats for transportation. Now that the spring flood season is approaching, the Yellow River water is rising and not receding. The submersion of the entire city is imminent. The disaster victims of the county will send representatives to the provincial capital to appeal for the rapid closure of the breach to save hundreds of thousands of lives. County Magistrate Zhang Qinglu has also telegraphed the province, reporting that the city walls are about to be submerged, and the entire county will be flooded imminently. He requests permission to relocate the county seat to another town, or else to continue to work on boats as in the worst of the floods in previous years. The provincial government is considering this and has not yet replied. Hu Yuanhui, Director of the Construction Department, rushed to the construction site before the lunar New Year due to the urgency of the breach closure project and has been stationed there for two months. The provincial government has repeatedly received his telegrams for help and has successively allocated 50,000 yuan for the project and 20,000 sacks for the closure. At the same time, 8,800 yuan were allocated to Changyuan County, with 5,000 yuan for reinforcing the Taihang embankment and 3,800 yuan for protecting the county seat. However, all efforts have failed. Recently, it was heard that Hu Yuanhui's opinions differ from those of Kong Xiangrong, Director of the Engineering and Relief Group of the Central Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee, and Hu is considering leaving the construction site and returning to the province. The provincial government believes that with the spring flood season approaching, this is a critical moment and should not allow anyone to be passive. Therefore, it telegraphed Chairman Yu Xuezhong in Beijing to report the situation. Yu telegraphed back yesterday. Although the original text did not explicitly comfort Hu, it encouraged the personnel at the construction site to work hard. The telegram reads as follows: "The Central Government has sent Vice Minister Fu Rulin to the construction site to supervise the closure. It is scheduled to depart from Beijing on the evening of the 9th. The current situation is extremely critical. For the sake of its duty, the Hebei Provincial Government has no room for shirking responsibility and must do its utmost to block the breach and quickly formulate a plan. All funds needed for the breach closure project will be borne by the Ministry, as clearly stated by the Central Government, and the Central Political Council has approved the raising of necessary funds. The Council has also been ordered to consult with the Ministry of Finance on relief measures. Therefore, the funding issue can be said to be no problem. If a firm decision is not made at this time and measures are not quickly taken, it will not only fail to live up to the Central Government, but also to the people. I believe that we must be responsible to the end no matter what. Please tell Brother Haimen (Hu Yuanhui) to overcome the difficulties. We are anxiously waiting." (11th)

Songjiang: Water Police Seize Smuggled Opium

Since Jiangsu Province implemented opium prohibition and a centralized opium control system, private sales have continued to flood the market, causing sluggish sales of government opium. Some officially licensed opium merchants have even suffered losses or insufficient income. Recently, Fan Zhicheng, captain of the First Squad of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team, received a tip-off that a well-known large-scale opium smuggler in Fengjing was smuggling a large quantity of privately produced opium to Zhujing via Shanghai. Captain Fan secretly investigated and successfully seized a sculling boat yesterday. The boatman confessed that the opium smugglers were A He and a certain Li. In addition to handing over the smuggled opium to the opium prohibition authorities for legal action, they are also investigating and arresting the opium smugglers for prosecution.

Octogenarian Woman Killed by Train

Yesterday (the 10th) afternoon, a third/fourth-class passenger train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, traveling upstream, struck an elderly woman in her eighties who was walking on Yang Bridge No. 29. She was knocked down, her left eye socket was crushed, her skull was fractured, and brain matter was flowing out, causing her death. The local town police reported the incident to the Third Sub-Precinct, which requested the court to conduct an examination. The family was ordered to collect the body for burial.

Suzhou: Labor Dispute Resolved at Silk Weaving Factory

The labor dispute at the Minsheng and other silk weaving factories, which lasted for half a month, was resolved on the afternoon of the 11th, when the county government convened a third mediation meeting. Five mediation measures were agreed upon: (1) Wages will be increased by 3 li (to 1.118 yuan per meter). (2) Workers who do not take leave on working days will be given a bonus of 1 jiao, apprentices 75% of that amount. (3) The apprenticeship period for apprentices over 20 years old shall not exceed three years, and for those under 20 years old, it will be extended by six months to one year. (4) The factory shall not dismiss representatives or workers and shall abolish employment contracts. (5) The cost of mending silk woven by workers shall be borne by the workers. Both labor and management were satisfied, and a settlement was reached.

Wuxi: Robberies Occur Continuously in Rural Areas

Due to the unrest and repeated robberies in rural areas, the root cause is the years of famine and rural bankruptcy. A summary is as follows: (1) In Yangwanli, near the town of Hudai in Fuan Township, residents of Su Zhihe's home were suddenly attacked by eight or nine bandits, speaking a mixture of Shanghai and Jiangbei dialects, who climbed over the wall and entered the house. They tied up Zhihe's parents and robbed them of over 100 yuan in leather coats and silver dollars. The bandits were not satisfied and went to Su Wenqi's house to rob, firing two shots as a warning. Fortunately, no one was injured. They were robbed of five or six yuan in silver dollars and over ten thousand copper coins. (2) At Shen Xilin's house, the Ba長 of Shangshuibin in Fangtao Township, in the Third District, more than twenty bandits broke into the house at midnight and robbed it. Shen Xilin was also injured in the waist and back with an iron ruler. Boxes in the house were pried open, and clothes and ornaments were robbed, resulting in a loss of 200 yuan. (3) The Tao Lane Elementary School in the same district was also visited by the bandits. The principal, Liu Guchu, had all his belongings robbed. Yesterday morning, the victims submitted loss reports to the county bureau requesting arrest.

Changzhou: Major Fire at Xie Feng Oil Factory

The Xie Feng Oil Factory, located on Nanheyan outside the West Gate, was founded by Xie Zijia, a local resident. It has been open for many years, is large in scale, and its business is one of the largest among oil factories. But at 0:30 this morning (the 12th), a fire suddenly broke out. Because it was all oil-related flammable materials, it spread extremely quickly. By the time the fire brigades from various districts arrived, it was difficult to extinguish due to the inconvenience of water supply. Except for the forward engine room, which was unscathed, the remaining hundred or so factory buildings were reduced to ashes. The thatched sheds outside the back door of the factory and the Jiangnan Ice Factory across the river were also burned down. The loss is estimated to be over 100,000 yuan. The fire was not extinguished until dawn.

Changshu: Secretary of Opium Prohibition Association Insists on Resignation

Gu Buzhai, the secretary of the Opium Prohibition Association, is a local resident who is responsible for handling opium addicts' self-surrender and issuing precepts. He finds the work to be heavy, and it is difficult for locals to handle local affairs without being influenced by emotions. Because he feels that handling the matter is difficult, he has repeatedly submitted his resignation to Zhai Yifu, the county magistrate and chairman of the committee. Because Gu is capable, Zhai has always comforted and encouraged him. Recently, Gu has insisted on resigning again. The county magistrate has not yet expressed his opinion.

Zhenjiang: Kidnapping and Robbery Occur in the Fourth District

Shen Gengbao, a resident of Donggou Village in the Fourth District, is a bookstore operator in Singapore. His wife, Jie, and a four-year-old girl live in the village, earning a living by farming. At 9 PM the other night, suddenly a group of bandits armed with weapons broke open the courtyard door and started robbing the place. Because there was not much cash, the bandits burned Jie with fire to force her to hand over silver dollars and kidnapped the girl. Jie was severely injured. In addition to reporting to the district office for arrest, she also hired laborers to carry her to the Pingmin Hospital in the city for treatment.

Nantong: Qijing Highway to be Completed Next Month

Zheng Yitong, the Nantong District Administrative Inspector, petitioned the provincial government to open the Qijing Highway to promote the prosperity of the counties north of the Yangtze River and connect it with the highways in northern Jiangsu. He also added a ferry between Jingjiang and Jiangyin to allow direct traffic between the north and south banks of the Yangtze River. The construction of the roadbed, bridges, and culverts is being undertaken by the counties through which the highway passes, while the road surface is being undertaken by the province. The work is currently underway and will be completed within the next month.

Hangzhou: Accident on Hangtang Road Passenger Bus

The Hangtang Road public bus, driven by driver Lu Qifa, was traveling from Hangzhou to Tangqi at 1:20 PM yesterday. Near Qiaosi Town, due to mechanical failure, the bus veered into a field, causing the bus to overturn. Six passengers, the driver, and the ticket seller were all injured. The driver was the most seriously injured. The Qiaosi station telegraphed the Highway Bureau to dispatch an ambulance to transport the injured back to the city and send them to Guangji Hospital for treatment. The passengers' injuries were minor, and they were all discharged from the hospital on the same day. However, the driver's injuries were serious, and he lost too much blood and was in a coma. He remained in the hospital for treatment.

Major Fire in Hangzhou's Baoyoufang

A fire broke out at 2:30 AM yesterday at the Dafeng Tiao Satin Bureau at No. 34 Baoyoufang in Hangzhou. The Provincial Public Security Bureau Fire Brigade and the United Fire Brigade of all sectors worked to extinguish the fire, which was put out after one hour. The cause of the fire is said to be negligence. The fire spread to the neighboring Hexinglong Wooden Comb and Mirror Box Shop and Watson's Pharmacy, causing losses of approximately 30,000 yuan.
