Li Jinxi Replies to Shu Xincheng Regarding Casting Phonetic Chinese Character Copper Molds

Discussion on the number of characters in the phonetic copper mold

The Ministry of Education is actively promoting mass education and compulsory education. A month ago, it sent a letter inviting Li Jinxi and Wang Yi, standing committee members of the National Language Unification Preparation Committee, to Beijing to discuss phonetic Chinese character copper molds and simplified characters. After Li and Wang investigated the situation of manufacturing phonetic Chinese character copper molds in Shanghai and submitted a written opinion to the ministry for review, the ministry approved it and handed it over to the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company for casting. Minister Wang Shijie submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval and approved the allocation of 20,000 yuan from the first reserve fund under the educational and cultural expenditure for this year to entrust Zhonghua with the casting. After that, all mass readings and primary school textbooks will be printed with phonetic Chinese characters. The plan was also resolved at the National Language Unification Conference on the 3rd of this month and submitted to the ministry for circulation. Shu Xincheng, director of the editing department of Zhonghua Book Company, sent a letter to discuss the limitation of the number of characters in the copper mold. Li Jinxi replied, deciding to cast 5,000 characters first and explaining the concerns of the general public. The original letter is recorded below:

Mr. Xincheng, I have received both of your letters. The issue of selecting the number of phonetic Chinese characters for the copper mold is indeed as you intended. There is no need to cast 10,000 or 8,000 characters in one go. I was about to reply when Director Zhang Xingfang sent a letter asking for my opinion on your intention. I replied immediately, as follows: "It is best to cast about four or five thousand characters first for the printing of primary school and mass education books and newspapers as the first batch (it is best to cast No. 3 size characters). The font material should be selected by Mr. Shu, sent to the ministry for review and decision. In this way, we can avoid prolonged delays. I agree very much. (However, the remaining characters should also be cast in the future, because even I couldn't read the correct pronunciation of many characters in the Three Capitals and Two Capitals in those years)." Today, I saw in the newspaper that at the 202nd meeting of the Executive Yuan on the 5th, Minister Wang proposed to entrust the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company to cast Chinese phonetic copper molds and drafted a contract, requesting approval to allocate 10,000 yuan from the first reserve fund under the educational and cultural expenditure for this year for working capital. The proposal was approved. This matter has now been finalized, so the number of characters should be decided urgently. According to your instructions, please select five thousand and five thousand to cast. Then this copper mold is enough for any purpose, or it must not be less than five thousand for any purpose. Although primary schools use only three thousand characters, and middle schools only four thousand, they not only read textbooks but also read books and reference books. I think that limiting the use of characters and defining "basic national language" are one thing, and casting phonetic font molds is another. The former is for writing, and the latter is for reading. How can reading be restricted? Children have talent, and the masses have outstanding talents. If they still want to freely read the Three Capitals and Two Capitals, what reason is there to restrict them? I think that one day the four major series published by your company will be rearranged using phonetic Chinese characters. This seems like a joke, but one day it will be done. Because the Three Capitals and Two Capitals have never had phonetic notations, and we have not been able to read them correctly. (In the past, teachers did not know how many character sounds they taught incorrectly. Now, it is not surprising that a large number of middle school and even university students read white characters. This must be verified in practice. Not to mention rare characters, even common characters are full of jokes. If you use the unified national pronunciation, the difference will be even greater.) If all are noted in the past, even children and the masses can at least read them correctly. (Not understanding the meaning is another matter, and being able to follow the phonetic apricot dictionary will completely solve the unsolvable problem of Chinese character retrieval and greatly open the way to white revision and broadcast the opportunity for culture.) As for writing, the number of characters must be limited. However, what is limited is Chinese characters, not phonetics. (Mr. Zhao Yuanren's work on basic national language is related to the principles of national language Romanization. The aims are not entirely the same. The resolution of the national language is also like this. Children and the masses do not need a thousand basic Chinese characters to write. The 3,420 characters of the Pingjiao Association are counted together with reading. If you only talk about writing, a thousand characters is enough. These thousand characters must be written in Chinese characters. Outside of a thousand characters, you can directly write in phonetics. If there are no thousand Chinese characters, you cannot adapt to the current living environment. Children and the masses can gradually write Chinese characters outside of a thousand characters from the publications they read, which is their intelligence. If there is no such intelligence, you can directly write in phonetics outside of a thousand characters. What is the harm of "single use and annotation of words in the mouth"? Mr. Show already cited the example of Confucius' kindergarten students in his second instruction. It is not necessary to limit it to kindergarten students. What is the harm if primary school students do this? What is the harm if the masses do this? Therefore, the number of phonetic Chinese character copper molds must be as large as possible, and limiting the number of basic characters is another matter, not to be discussed together. Therefore, five thousand characters are the first batch, and the second batch should be cast as previously discussed, casting all 9,920 characters in the Commonly Used Vocabulary of National Sounds. The third batch is for the Three Capitals and Two Capitals and is designed for reprinting the four major series. When you are ready to cast the second batch, I will go south again and ask the ministry for funding. At this time, please rush to make the first batch of 5,000 characters to benefit the masses, enlighten children, and benefit scholars. The issues shown in the second letter are even more serious. You think that "students above the third grade of elementary school do not need to use phonetic Chinese characters except for new characters." Using the simple score and the original score of music songs as an analogy, I am afraid that if the simple score is attached, it will not be easy to change to the original score in the future. I will also say nonsense that "the metaphor is not successful." Phonetic symbols can be compared to a simple score, but it is not possible to compare Chinese characters to the original score. Chinese characters are the old gongche score. Annotating Chinese characters with phonetics is annotating gongche with a simple score, not annotating the original score with a simple score. Those who learn Kunqu opera and pihuang opera actually use gongche scores. We should recognize this fact. For the sake of convenience and correctness in learning, we attach a more scientific simple score. This is progress and is gradually becoming a fact. After practicing Kunqu opera and pihuang opera well according to this simple score, you can blow, pull, sing, and perform. The purpose has been achieved. Then why bother about gongche scores? "The trap is used to catch fish. Once you get the fish, forget the trap." Writing is a tool to introduce knowledge and skills, develop thoughts and emotions, and even convey national culture. The tool must be rationalized so that it is easy to get the fish. The purpose is only to get the fish. Today, most Chinese people think that "I would rather not get the fish than forget the trap," or think that the sign is the fish. The Ding County experiment report said that they mistakenly regarded Chinese characters as the knowledge and culture itself, and did not know that it was just a tool (see page 418 of the Outline of National Language History). The Chinese character problem looks serious, but it is actually very easy. You only need to compare it to the gongche score, relax, and annotate it with a simple score. The concerns you have can be dispelled. Therefore, I respectfully follow your advice and expand it slightly. (1) All mass readings are printed in phonetic Chinese characters (as you advise). (2) Part of the readings for kindergarten students and first-grade elementary school students are completely in phonetic symbols (as you advise, please ask your bureau to compile them as soon as possible. For the compilation method, please refer to pages 434,445,152 of the preface to my book Outline of the History of the National Language Movement, which are my simple opinions. I also have detailed designs for kindergarten students to practice phonetic symbols and for first-grade elementary school students to write. Please refer to pages 176,191 of my new book National Language Teaching Method). (3) All textbooks for each subject in the six years of elementary school are printed in phonetic Chinese characters. (4) All extracurricular reading materials for children are printed in phonetic Chinese characters. The above points have been passed as a proposal at the Standing Committee of the National Language Association on the 3rd of this month and submitted to the ministry for review and implementation. Another case is a regulation on the method of specifying the phonetic style, which is attached in two mimeographed copies. You have shown the layer of field trials shown at the end. Over the past ten years, the National Language Association has accumulated reports in various aspects, so it dares to affirm and asks it to be enacted as an order. If you want to do a thorough experiment again, the only prerequisite is to have beautifully printed books and newspapers with phonetic Chinese characters. Otherwise, there is no way to start. However, making more copper molds and widely printing readings with phonetic Chinese characters is still an urgent task in education, not a strong edict of the law. I hope you will plan for it.

Municipal Education Bureau Edits Municipal Literacy Textbooks

Divided into four-month and two-month versions. Principles for two-month textbooks are determined.

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau has organized an editing committee for mass school textbooks and appointed Jiang Shuxun, Chen Bai, Zhang Zhu, Mei Changjia, Shi Lianhuang, Shi Chongpeng, Li Wanyu, Wu Shiqian, Xie Meisun, Ji Xiaobo, Hu Changcai, Su Baogen, and Chen Songchun as members. The mass school textbooks compiled are divided into two types: a four-month version for mass schools and a two-month version for literacy classes. For the two-month version, the following principles were determined at the first editing meeting: (1) Naming: The textbook is named "Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Literacy Textbook." (2) Number of lessons: Six lessons per week, eight reviews, and the remaining time for general review. (3) Word range: The vocabulary compiled by the Mass Education Section is mimeographed into fifteen copies and distributed. Each member subjectively determines 600 words, and then selects the 600 words that appear the most frequently among those determined by the fifteen members as the word range of this textbook. (4) Lesson content: Temporarily divided into four items: civics, nature, society, and hygiene. Civics has sixteen lessons, nature has twelve lessons, society has twelve lessons, and hygiene has eight lessons. Member Li Wanyu will propose topics and submit them for discussion at the next meeting. (5) Lesson style: Mainly in vernacular, rhyming, and simple text. (6) Pictures: Distinguish between new words and the general meaning of the text. (Those that can be expressed in pictures are expressed in pictures.) The order of various aspects is determined by the four members Zhang Meisun, Ji Xiaobo, Shi Chongpeng, and Shi Lianhuang. (7) Textbook classification: There is no need to edit separately for farmers, workers, and women (select) a common vocabulary for public application.

Wang Jiyuan Returns to Shanghai to Discuss the Exhibition in the Philippines

Filipinos Have Limited Knowledge of Chinese Art, President of the Philippine University's Art Academy Exchanges a Painting, and Plans to Send Students to China to Study Art

Mr. Wang Jiyuan, Vice President of the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts, has completed his trip to the Philippines to hold a Chinese modern calligraphy and painting exhibition. He returned to Shanghai with the tourist group to the Philippines a few days ago. A Shanghai News Agency reporter specially visited Mr. Wang at his residence yesterday to learn about the exhibition and the art situation in the Philippines. The exhibition's progress, according to Mr. Wang, was aimed at communicating Chinese and Filipino culture, fostering friendship with neighboring countries, and raising funds to build a new campus for the art academy. A total of 300 calligraphy and painting works were brought and exhibited at the Manila Oriental Club and the Chinese Youth Association on the 13th of last month. On the opening day, consuls from various countries attended the ceremony, which was quite grand. The number of visitors was also exceptionally crowded. The exhibition was originally scheduled to close on the 18th, but it was extended to the 23rd at the request of various circles. About 200 paintings and calligraphy works were sold, and the remaining pieces were managed by the Overseas Chinese Education Association.

Art in the Philippines: The Philippines has only made progress in culture in the last hundred years, so its art is quite immature. Due to the lack of promotion of Chinese art in the Philippines in the past, its understanding is quite limited. There were questions about calligraphy and light ink paintings because of their simple colors and high prices. This is generally evident. Their understanding of Western painting is also very immature. The style is from the 17th century, with European colors still passed down by the Spanish. Therefore, in terms of new and artistic styles, China is ahead of the Philippines. Furthermore, it is difficult to find paper, ink, brushes, and inkstones for Chinese calligraphy and painting. Most of the interior decorations in civilian homes are enlarged photographs in frames for hanging, with no calligraphy or paintings. Therefore, after holding the exhibition in the Philippines this time, it has left a deep impression on the Filipinos.

Philippine University Art Academy: The Art Academy of the University of the Philippines is the highest institution for studying art in the Philippines. Its buildings and scale are quite grand. The Dean, Lilaroso, is a famous figure in the Philippines. The school studies Western painting, not Chinese painting. There are also two or three Chinese students studying at the school, but because their parents are engaged in business in the Philippines, they study commercial applied arts, sculpture patterns, and the like. I visited the school and found that both male and female students must wear clothes, which shows their backward thinking. However, music, dance, and drama are quite developed.

Exchange of Paintings: The Dean of the Art Academy of the University of the Philippines exchanged a framed Western painting with Wang Jiyuan's "Landscape and Wild Rain Picture." The exchange ceremony was presided over by the President of the University of the Philippines, Bugobo. This is the starting point of Chinese-Philippine cultural exchange. The painting of the Dean is now stored in the library of the University of the Philippines, and the painting of Wang Jiyuan is stored in the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts. The University of the Philippines also plans to send students to China to study Eastern culture. The general comment on Chinese painting after this exhibition was: "Flowers represent the four seasons of China, ladies and gentlemen represent the ethnic costumes of Chinese dynasties, and landscapes represent the transcendence of Chinese national thought, and the hanging of Chinese paintings from top to bottom is a sign of transcendence."

Cultural Construction Monthly, Issue 6, Published

Rich and Comprehensive Cultural News

In the past two months, two events in China's cultural circles have been most noteworthy. One is the declaration of the Ten Professors on January 10th, advocating the establishment of a Chinese-based culture with an attitude of not clinging to the old and not blindly following. The other is the reading competition initiated by the China Cultural Construction Association, hoping to create a good learning atmosphere. Regarding these two events, the former occurred earlier and has now reached an important stage of development. The latter, although it happened recently, has also made considerable progress. Detailed information is included in the recently published Volume 1, Issue 6 of the Cultural Construction Monthly. This issue includes a record of the Capital Chinese-Based Cultural Construction Symposium, recording the opinions of people in the capital's cultural circles on the construction of a Chinese-based culture. There is a Chinese Culture Discussion section, such as Li Jianfang's "Characteristics of Chinese Cultural Development," Zhang Jinjian's "Special Qualities of Chinese Culture," Fan Zhongyun's "A Discussion on Chinese Cultural Construction from the History of Cultural Development," and Shen Yan's "Review of the Problem of Restoring the Inherent Culture," discussing Chinese culture, each with unique insights. There is "The Origin of the Reading Competition," detailing the purpose of the China Cultural Construction Association's initiation of this event and methods for encouraging reading. The beginning of the volume also includes a call for submissions advertisement for Chinese-based cultural construction and a membership solicitation advertisement for the Reading Competition. All those who wish to understand the progress of the two major events in China's cultural circles recently and who wish to obtain submission prizes and reading prizes should purchase and read it as soon as possible, as sales of the publication have recently surged, and delays may lead to regret. It is heard that starting from Volume 1, Issue 7, the content and form of the publication will be further refined to meet the elegant expectations of readers.

Third China Vocational Supplementary School: The Third China Vocational Supplementary School, established by the China Vocational Education Society on Lujiabang Road outside Xiaoximen, offers courses in mechanical and electrical engineering, architectural drawing, and English, all taught in the evening, allowing aspiring youth to make use of their spare time for further studies. The courses offered are particularly needed at present, so they have received considerable attention from society. It is heard that the number of students in the mechanical and electrical engineering courses has increased significantly this semester, and the courses have been divided into advanced and beginner levels. Furthermore, the number of applicants has continued to increase in recent days. It is also heard that the school, in view of the general lack of knowledge in mathematics and science among students and youth, will add a Sunday mathematics and science class to allow them to study on Sundays.

The Two Rivers Basketball Team's Southern Expedition Record (3)

Thirty-Five to Fourteen - A Great Victory Over the Philippine Island Allied Forces

(Manila Communication) Since arriving in the Philippines, the Two Rivers team has won repeatedly, and the overseas Chinese community is proud. There has been a warm welcome. Last month, because the Philippine Islands were holding the National Games and the top athletes had to attend the National Games, and the Lim Long court was also in use, the second cycle was delayed until February 27th. The game started at 8:00 PM. The Lim Long court was filled with spectators. According to the Philippine Allied Forces, it is a strong and powerful team formed by the Philippines and the United States. The Philippine sprinter, Au Qika, who will attend the World Games, also participated in the competition. His sprints were unmatched throughout the stadium, and his shooting was also accurate. He is the cornerstone of the Philippine Allied Forces. The strength is quite strong, causing the overseas Chinese audience to worry about the Two Rivers team. The tension of the battle was expected. The game started at 8:00 PM, and the battle was very tense. Because Pan Meng committed two fouls, the Min team launched a strong attack and opened the scoring. The three Chens of the Two Rivers team were not willing to be outdone. They worked together to break the duck egg. From then on, both sides were cautious and fought for points. Bao Shuxia blocked and dribbled the ball, and Hu Zuoqiong accelerated and galloped. In a flash, the score gradually increased. You were brave and I was fierce. The first half ended with the Two Rivers team leading 14 to 8. After the break, the team made a comeback. The Two Rivers team finally used its experience and rapid passing, five tigers attacking, and effective defense. The score soared. The Allied Forces gradually showed exhaustion and could not catch up. The Two Rivers team completed the hegemony with a score of 35 to 14 in one go. Later, the entire Min team invited the Two Rivers team to the Great East Restaurant for a banquet to strengthen friendship.

(B) Regarding the preparation for the demonstration meet, it was resolved that (1) the original draft be revised and passed; (2) Yuan Zhiren, Ma Yuehan, Dong Shouyi, Li Zhou, Liu Quan, Zhang Shouyi, Wang Jingzhi, and Xu Chonghou be appointed as preparatory committee members, convened by Li Zhou. (C) Regarding the request from the Senior Commercial and Vocational School for the allocation of a sports ground, it was resolved that Committee Member Li Zhou conduct a survey and then hand it over to the Social Affairs Bureau for handling. (D) Regarding the National Martial Arts Hall's proposed construction plan for a martial arts field, it was resolved that it be handed over to the sports field preparatory committee to be handled together with the aforementioned case. (E) Regarding the drafting of the sports administration plan for the 24th year, it was resolved that Li Zhou draft it first. (F) Regarding the preparation for the summer training course for physical education teachers in primary and secondary schools, it was resolved that (1) a summer training course for physical education teachers in primary and secondary schools be held first; (2) the training methods be drafted by Li Zhou and incorporated into the summer training course for primary school teachers.

Demonstration Plan: (1) Dates: (A) Set for May 10th, 11th, and 12th, a total of three days. (B) The mornings of the 10th and 11th will be the time for the demonstration meet; the afternoons of the 11th and the 12th will be the time for track and field events. (2) Location: Tentatively set at the city's public sports field. If preparation is insufficient, it will remain at the Municipal Fourth Middle School sports field. (3) Expenses: The preparatory committee will draft the budget, and after it is passed by the general meeting, it will be submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and allocation. (4) Events: (A) Primary School Section: (1) Demonstration lessons, to be attended by fifth-grade students (if there are only four grades, then fourth-grade students will attend), with each school allocated thirty minutes. The program should follow the curriculum standards and detailed teaching materials promulgated by the bureau, with a number of students ranging from twenty-five to forty. (2) Track and field events are open to voluntary participation. The events will be determined by the preparatory committee and announced after being approved by the general meeting. (B) Secondary School Section: (1) Introductory demonstration program, freely selected and practiced, with a duration of thirty minutes (mandatory participation, attended by second-year students, with a number of students ranging from twenty-five to forty). The introductory track and field events will be determined by the preparatory committee. (2) Advanced track and field events. (C) University and open track and field events (Note: For girls' track and field events, junior high school is introductory level, and senior high school is advanced level). (5) No trophies will be awarded at this primary and secondary school demonstration meet (all participants will be given commemorative certificates).

New York Stock Market Affected by Cotton

Uniform Plunge: Record New Low for the Year

Xinfeng Foreign Company reported that yesterday (the 11th), the New York stock market saw heavy selling pressure, and prices plunged, reaching a new low for the year. The market was affected by the sharp fall in cotton. The fall in cotton was entirely due to rumors, especially rumors that the government's cotton loan would not continue. Agricultural stocks were among the hardest hit, as they are directly related to the reduction in income for cotton farmers. Another reason for the stock market decline, and one that particularly affected gold and silver stocks, was the Ministry of Finance's recall of government bonds, which naturally led to the cancellation of banknotes issued by federally chartered banks. Wall Street speculators recognized this as further proof of the government's avoidance of inflation. The bond market and small exchanges followed other markets downstream, and grains were also affected by the same factors. The total trading volume for the day was 800,000 shares. Metals – Large Bars of Pig Lead Arrive, Sales Stagnant

The market for large bars of pig lead has been sluggish recently. Although the new tea season is approaching, the silver market is currently tight. Furthermore, the sales of tea last year by foreign firms were not good, resulting in poor results. Therefore, they are unwilling to lend generously to tea merchants this year. The demand from paint companies, red lead factories, and type-casting workshops is limited because they purchased too much last time. The overall market is soft due to poor sales. However, the arrival of goods is abundant, leading to large stockpiles. The standard price has fallen from 14.34 yuan to 14 yuan. Hunan native lead has also been affected by the sluggish sales of foreign lead, with the current market price at 13.34 yuan. It is estimated that only forty to fifty bars have been traded.

Oil Market – White Tung Oil Continues to Rise in Hankou

Since the surge in white tung oil last week, the situation has become increasingly stable. Hankou dealers added to the price, selling at 35.40 yuan per picul according to foreign regulations. By last week, the price stabilized. After entering this week, the market has risen again. According to reports from Hankou in the past two days, foreign firms have been buying at over 36 yuan. This high price has not been seen since the adoption of the foreign exchange standard and is the highest in the last three or four years. According to Hankou firms, inventories are extremely low, making it difficult for foreign firms stationed in Hankou to purchase large quantities. Recently, Hankou firms have gradually increased the number of inbound cargo ships. Xiangyang tung oil has been traded at around 29 yuan, and southern branch tung oil is even above 29 yuan, both according to customer regulations. This is because Xiangyang tung oil had a slightly lower density due to the weather last winter, so the selling price was cheaper than southern branch tung oil, which is also a change in the market. Zhejiang tung oil has also risen along with the Hankou market. It is reported that the price of standard density oil in Hangzhou has increased to over 33 yuan. Although there are no large-scale transactions for foreign firms in this port, sporadic purchases of thirty to fifty tons are still heard from time to time. This is because Shanghai's exports rely entirely on Zhejiang tung oil, and the output of Zhejiang province is insufficient to supply such a large volume of foreign sales. Therefore, firms in this port engaged in direct export trade are afraid to pre-sell large quantities.

The price of thick indica rice continued to depreciate by five cents, and although there were sudden purchases of a thousand or so bags of late rice such as Yantai Weihaiwei, the market also saw a step-by-step increase of several cents. The price of nearly new, Du Yang tip rice was unchanged due to similar supply and demand.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, few boats arrived from various routes along the river, about ten or so. Sales of various goods on the market were average. Medium-grade white indica rice was scarce, causing the price to rise by ten cents. The market price of thin rice was slightly down by a small number of cents in the afternoon, and the prices of other goods were also slightly stable. However, the price of white yuan rice sold for retail purposes was increased by five or six cents.

Page 16

Free Talk

On Activist Literature

— Zhang Xiangshan

Since André Malraux received the Prix Goncourt, activist literature has gained worldwide attention, and his masterpiece, "Man's Fate" (La Condition Humaine), has become a favorite among readers. Some have compared the value of this book to the only stinging creation since Nietzsche.

The rise of activist literature in today's literary world is an excellent reflection of the global trend among the intellectual class, especially as it emerges from the world of pure art. It is particularly significant and flavorful to see it emerge in the French literary world, known for its fragrant artistic atmosphere.

As a result of World War I, the French intellectual class suffered an incurable spiritual blow. Therefore, in postwar France, despair dominated the intellectual class, along with a fondness for mysterious, bizarre, and unrealistic psychology. This ideology continued to be maintained along with the relative prosperity under the stable French franc.

Recently, due to the intensification of the global panic, the general middle class in France has deeply felt that life is mired in a quagmire. This "life hardship" has caused everyone to jump out of the swamp of despair and seek a way out for themselves, as seen in the cases of André Gide and Fernandez.

In this situation, the general intellectual class abandoned liberalism and began to advocate and promote activism. These so-called activists advocate a positive and affirmative attitude to replace a negative and rejecting one. They not only observe but also value action. Furthermore, activism advocates that action is the overflow of the entire life.

This activism has certain limits, which can be said to be its foundation, built on the philosophy of Henri Bergson. This may be an overstatement, but at least this activism is indeed related to Bergson's philosophy. Bergson's philosophy is the "philosophy of life." He said that "reality" never repeats itself but is an endless stream of life that is constantly created and transformed. However, thinking abstracts this concrete reality of endless flow and turns it into something fixed. So-called matter is merely a fixed state of the flow of life. The dualism of mind and matter can be unified by the monism of consciousness, so the concept of "élan vital" is at the core of his thought. The error in this philosophy is very obvious. Therefore, French activist literature, guided by this philosophy, cannot completely settle the past nihilism, blind faith, and Fauvism.

Activism is often misunderstood, or rather, it is often used to whitewash one's own depravity. Although French activism is not yet perfect, it is at least a valuable product of the intellectual class's attempt to rescue themselves from a state of doubt and self-abandonment. However, this activism often falls into the hands of a few people, who treat it as a panacea for the intellectual class. Because the intellectual class is a middle layer, many people strongly emphasize the so-called "special qualities" of the intellectual class, its dynamism. This dynamism can be understood as "doing as one pleases" and standing in a "guiding position." Although "doing as one pleases" has some limitations, namely, being limited to following the correct direction of history, this is self-justification and still the old liberalism. As for "guiding position," to put it clearly, it means standing in a guiding position. This attempt to establish the omnipotent status of the intellectual class by borrowing the banner of activism simply dismembers activism.

True activism, as I said above, replaces a negative and rejecting attitude with a positive and affirmative one. Not only that, but it must also abandon Bergson's "philosophy of life" and build on a correct worldview. Although all current realities are very complex and unfree, the trajectories of pursuing contradictions are all similar. Therefore, I believe that it is also possible for human beings to engage in mutual social criticism. In this situation, it is necessary to fully recognize the regressive historical trends. The social movement and progress follow the steady progress of the intellectual class and present a new posture. By reversing the heavy pressure added to oneself, one can better obtain the practical action of seeking truth.

Here, let's talk about activist literature again! So-called activist literature can simply be called literature full of the spirit of activism. The author's own unease and the images of various real-world sufferings are not merely materials for the writer to think about but can be used as materials for the writer to organize, analyze, and practice. André Malraux once said at a lecture: "If the writer is a skilled technician, we must never forget that the highest function of the technician is invention. Art is not obedience; art is a conqueror." At the same time, in his maiden work, "The Conquerors," he simply compared himself to a conqueror. In this thought, we can see the promotion of better development of art, and in this, fully express the passion to approach the reality of society and one's own artistic claims.

Activist literature does not contain extremely mechanical political meaning, but it is also not Bogdanov's culturalism. It tears apart and abandons the attitude of isolating the author from reality and thoroughly experiences reality. It is not merely experiencing but using the rich knowledge of the intellectual class to do the work of analysis and dissection. We believe that with the outstanding ability of the intellectual class, coupled with their practical experience, the achievements of this struggle for all truth are indeed remarkable. The writer who holds this activist spirit and produces creations for the expression of all images will inevitably be able to truly reflect reality and have progressive qualities.

Jiangnan Park

— Nishimura

Jiangnan Park gets its name because the park site is located on the south bank of the Songhua River, opposite the city of Jilin and the area of Sandao Pier on the north bank.

Jiangnan Park is unique in that it does not charge admission fees. Thinking about it, I guess all the parks in Northeast China don't charge admission fees, right? Only in this way is it truly a "public" park, a "public" park in name and in fact. Otherwise, a "public" park watched by police at the gate, where no one can enter without a ticket, should actually be a "private" park.

The way to get to Jiangnan Park is to take a boat from Sandao Pier. This kind of boat is specially used for ferrying between Jiangnan and Jiangbei, but it's not a sampan like in the south. It's called a "Little Weihu," long and narrow with pointed ends instead of square ones. To give an analogy, if you cut a long, thin cucumber in half lengthwise and remove the seeds, that's a miniature "Little Weihu."

The park gate faces north and can be seen from the boat. But the plaque on the gate doesn't say "Jiangnan Park." This used to be an agricultural experiment station, and the old sign hasn't been removed yet.

Around the park gate, there are some vendors selling snacks, stalls, melons, soda, and tea are the main items, and cigarettes and sugar balls are also indispensable. There is also a "talking box" in the teahouse. Sometimes this thing opens its big mouth and shouts randomly for a while, and sometimes it emits a delicate and charming female voice, which can attract the attention of some tourists.

After entering the park, the usual practice is to walk east along the willow-shaded path, but in my opinion, it's better to go west, turn south, and pass through some fruit trees, where you can see some wild animals. There is also a basketball court and parallel bars here, where athletes and martial arts masters can show off their skills. Two rows of old houses exude a strong musty smell, which may evoke a sense of aging.

Turning back to the east, you'll arrive in front of a two-story hall. This is where the director of the agricultural experiment station used to work. If you know the director and plan to host friends and relatives in the park, the hall can be borrowed, and it's free. But there is no restaurant or snack shop here, so you must bring all the food and drink with you from Jiangnan. The windows of the building are level with the willow branches. Looking into the distance, the south is a flat field, and behind it winds a series of mountains. To the east, the Immortal Cave area is a belt of low hills, but behind the hills, a series of high mountains still emerge. The Songhua River flows from the southwest and turns to the northeast, reflecting the mountains and hills, and set against the azure sky, your gaze will evoke some pleasure.

Exiting the east gate of the agricultural experiment station, there is a small flower garden to the north outside the gate. If you say you're here to stroll through the park, it's better to say you're here to stroll through the flower garden. Upon entering the flower garden, there is a pool of water with a layer of lotus leaves floating on it. Outside the pool are square flower beds. Behind the flower beds is a long row of greenhouses, partially built underground, with roofs covered entirely in glass, which is where the flowers are kept in the winter.

In the flower garden, as far as the eye can see, there are all kinds of flowers, which are extremely beautiful. The fragrance floats in the air, bees and butterflies fly among the flowers, and people in this situation cannot but feel the beauty of nature.

Two thatched pavilions stand in the flower bushes, dilapidated and tilted, so mismatched with the competing flower bushes! Ivy climbs from all over the pavilion along the ropes tied to the roof, all the way to the top of the pavilion, often blocking the wind that blows through the holes in the pavilion.

Behind the pavilion is a grove of poplars, and outside the grove is a sandy beach, with red and green intertwined, and the sparkling river water, which is quite an interesting scene.

Leaving the flower garden and heading east is the woodland area. From the nameplates, you can learn what is called German locust, what is called American poplar, and some other trees. I would rather stroll under the trees than admire the flowers in the flower garden. The gorgeous and fragrant flowers are not as good as the majestic and aloof woodland area.

Having walked here, you have already walked the entire garden. It's time to go back to the city. Walking a few more steps east, you can cross the river from Xiaodongmen to the opposite bank of the wave mouth and return to the city.

Climbing Mount Jing

— Shen Shengshi

In Huaiyuan, Mount Jing and Mount Tu are somewhat famous. It is said that Mount Tu is even more desolate. Since it is desolate, one must go and play in a desolate place once! In China, desolate places and barren mountains are everywhere! I want to find another opportunity to also go and see the desolate Mount Tu.

That day, we went to Mount Jing, four of us together, walking from the streets of Huaiyuan. Before long, we arrived at the foot of the mountain.

Although the sky was overcast, our mood for climbing the mountain was sunny.

On the mountainside, we found a mountain spring. The spring water was milky white. Above the spring, a stone was carved with the two red characters "Milky Spring." The characters were vigorous and powerful, but there was no date or name of the calligrapher to be found. Next to the spring, in a clearing under the shade of the trees, an ancient-looking Taoist was fanning the fire next to a stove. The water was from the Milky Spring. Every day, he scooped up the milky white water from the spring, one bamboo tube after another, to make tea. The Taoist's life is finite. Could he possibly scoop the Milky Spring dry?

Climbing up the mountainside to the Wanghuai Tower, the architecture of the tower was not at all elegant, fitted with dilapidated glass windows, neither Chinese nor Western. What does it look like? It's really hard to say. Inside the tower were placed tea tables, chairs, and couches, and the walls were covered with couplets. At the time, I read them all once, but when I came back, I couldn't remember them halfway, except that I remembered that the lower half of one couplet had "Su Zi came to visit." Checking the local chronicles, Su Dongpo, the witty and eccentric figure from the Song Dynasty, had also visited. Mount Jing is still the Mount Jing of those days, but our poet has long turned to dust! A little bit of sorrow touched my heart.

Wanghuai Tower, as the name suggests, tells you that climbing the tower to look at the Huai River is the best thing to do. There is a short railing in front of the tower. Leaning on the railing, you send your gaze into the distance. The Huai River's thousand miles of sparkling waves, the sails on the water standing like a forest, the whistles of small steamships, drifting leisurely in the wind. In this situation, you can't help but praise the magnificence of the mountains and rivers.

I looked down the Huai River. I looked at the boundless horizon, looking until the end of the earth, unable to see my hometown in the south! Some smoky sorrows struck my heart. I suddenly remembered a fragmented sentence from Du Fu.

—Across the sea, the brothers are separated by the dust of war,

At the end of the earth, tears and snot, just myself, alone and far!

The Taoist on the mountain brought up the tea brewed from the Milky Spring. The tea was fragrant and clear, but we were vulgar people who didn't understand how to appreciate tea. In our hectic lives, could we possibly have the mood of an "elegant person"?

The clouds of dusk blurred the sky. We didn't have the courage to climb the high peak.

February 23, 1935, in Huaiyuan.

Hater of Servility (Cont. 2)

— Cao Ming

"I told you, she could go a whole day without speaking. My little daughter was always out playing in the streets, and at that time, I had learned to speak to women very softly and gently, so you could hear the chickens clucking in the house, but no human voices. Alas, if it weren't for that festering sore on my leg, maybe I'd have a little more respect for the women now!" He sighed, then started to calculate the days in his head, and continued... "That sore festered for five months, and I couldn't move at all. The money ran out. My second wife and daughter, just like when they first came, had faces like vegetable leaves from the trash can, covered with worried wrinkles. I'd often pat the bed and tell her to relax: "What's the big deal?... When everyone can't move anymore, we'll all just lie in bed together."...

"Finally, one day, I shouted myself hoarse, but they didn't even bother to look at me, and they never came back..."

His hand, clutching the chopsticks, was raised in the air, trembling in space as if he couldn't put it down. His gray eyes were full of cruel, cold light. Anger drove the old man – his crazed eyes fixed on something on the wall, his arms spread open, slowly and terribly lifting his swollen body. Some of the unclear "heh-heh" sounds that old people often make rolled out of his throat. This action continued for a short while, then he suddenly sat down as if someone had hit him, and then laughed as calmly and emotionlessly as usual.

As I was leaving, I handed him a penny and asked him for a handful of green onions. He casually put the penny in his pocket, picked up the pot, used the tip of his chopsticks to stir the embers in the stove that were almost extinguished, then took another deep sip of wine and smacked his lips in appreciation of the liquor.

But a few steps after I left the door, the old man suddenly shouted loudly from behind:

"Hey, where's the money? You haven't given me the money for the green onions yet." His corroded memory had completely forgotten that he had received the money, and he waved to me anxiously. I walked further away, and I could still vaguely hear him muttering curses... (The End)

Raffle

Those Hanlin Scholars and Jinshi Graduates are All Useless Treasures (2)

— Cao Jurein

Why is it that among those who passed the imperial examinations, none of them truly understood ancient books? The reason is simple: if one truly understood ancient books, one would have no hope of passing the imperial examinations. For example, in the *Analects*, "Confucius said: 'In matters of benevolence, one should not defer even to one's teacher.'" The commentary by Kong Anguo states: "When performing acts of benevolence, one should not defer even to one's teacher, indicating the urgency of practicing benevolence." However, those who read the *Analects* from then on only interpreted "teacher" as "master." During the Northern Song Dynasty, a scholar taking the examination used the old commentary from the Han Dynasty, interpreting it as "In matters of benevolence, one should not defer even to the masses," which was a better interpretation, but he failed the examination because of it. Another example is the line from the *Analects*: "The gentleman is ashamed of his words exceeding his actions." Zhu Xi's commentary states: "Ashamed means not daring to covet; exceeding means desiring to have more than enough." This is clearly a case of interpreting the text literally and talking nonsense. During the Qing Dynasty, a scholar, based on the imperial edition and the Korean edition, corrected the error of "之" in place of "而," but he also failed the examination because of it. You see, if one truly seeks to understand ancient books, how dangerous it is for passing the imperial examinations; having truly understood ancient books, one should never hope to be among those who passed the imperial examinations! When I was young, my father and teacher taught me to read the *Four Books*, only allowing me to read Zhu Xi's commentary and not allowing me to read the Qing Dynasty scholars' textual research. Once, I read He Yan's commentary on the *Analects* and used it to refute Zhu Xi's commentary, and I even received a big thump on the head from my late father! Only now do I understand that they hoped I would not truly understand ancient books to avoid trouble, which was actually a kind intention! With this kind of way of reading ancient books, where "predecessors fart, and successors say it smells good," how can one possibly understand them? Even if Confucius were resurrected, he could only be a fool, right?

Some people think that the top graduates (Zhuangyuan) are always literary stars from heaven, with ten or eight *dou* of talent; presumably, they get this idea from operas and plays. But in reality, the rankings of the top five in the palace examination (commonly referred to as *Zhuangyuan*, *Tanhua*, etc.) are decided early on by the backers who are in the know (the story goes that anyone who hopes to be among the top three are all pulled in as disciples by nobles in the court). The quality of the writing has nothing to do with it. Palace examination essays have a fixed range of topics, and the number of words is limited by the emperor's decree, so "newcomers from the grass roots" are never allowed to express any opinions. In palace examination papers, the level of the opening lines and the words to be avoided are much more important than the quality of the writing. Among the six hundred *Zhuangyuan*, we have never seen any works of lasting value passed down. Not only are there no works of lasting value, but if the *Zhuangyuan* later truly studies and is able to write something, he will undoubtedly feel like vomiting for three days after reading his own palace examination paper—that's how useless the *Zhuangyuan* are.

Below the level of *Zhuangyuan*, such as *Juren*, *Jinshi*, and Hanlin scholars, it goes without saying that they "do not understand ancient books" and their "writing is poor." As the predecessors said, "Don't discuss literature in the examination hall." The standard for judging essays in the examination hall is the correctness of the calligraphy and the appropriateness of the format, which has nothing to do with the quality of the essay itself. Jiang Chenying, a classical prose writer of the early Qing Dynasty, was highly respected for a time, and Wei Shuzi praised him as being "among the purest and most sincere." However, he failed the examinations several times because his writing deviated from the formal requirements of the examination hall. Later, he took the examination at the Ministry of Rites and again violated the format. The examiner, unwilling to lose such a talent, corrected his paper, and he finally became a *Jinshi*. This was only because the Kangxi Emperor intentionally helped him succeed; otherwise, wouldn't he have remained a scholar all his life? Below the level of *Juren*, such as *Xiucai* and *Gongsheng*, it is exactly like:

"Three sentences to answer the question, two sentences to break the question, wagging your head and shaking your body, you are a high-ranking disciple of the sage. But do you know what kind of writing it is to pass three or four times, and which dynasty did Han Gaozu and Tang Taizong belong to? On the desk is a tall lecture, and in the shop, one buys the latest examination aids. Reading it makes one's shoulders high and low, and one's mouth sighs. Chewing sugarcane dregs over and over, what flavor is there? Wasting time, one is confused for a lifetime. Even if he deceives himself into high office, it is bad luck for the people and the court." – Xu Lingtai: *Hui Xi Dao Qing*. There is no need to talk about reading and understanding ancient books and literature.

Spring and Autumn Annals

Tidbits

— (Shen Shouruo)

Now is a world of scientific civilization, and everything has standard inventions: such as standard beauties, standard cigarettes, standard time, etc., which are said to be the best achievements of scientific civilization. However, the lack of something that science cannot remedy is that there is no standard invention for the human heart!

I think the saying "Everything requires patience" should be differentiated: things that are trivial and without value to haggle over, patience is acceptable: things that are important and have value to haggle over, patience is not acceptable. However, when my negotiating power is not strong enough, and I anticipate not getting a victory, I must also endure temporarily, preparing my strength to seize the opportunity to win: it is not to say that everything, regardless of size, should be met with patience and without haggling.

The inkstone heart was not originally black, but because of its proximity to the ink, it became black as well! As the saying goes: "One who is near vermilion gets stained red, and one who is near ink gets stained black." If one is not careful, one will be influenced. When we conduct ourselves in society, we must also take this as a warning and guard against the temptations of all colors!

Dream Talk

— Hua Binghe

I often have fantasies, assuming that I could be like Chunyu Fen in "The Story of the Governor of Nanke," becoming the son-in-law of the king of the Huai'an Kingdom and the governor of Nanke County, allowing a poor boy to vent his anger. Although it is a spring dream, everything in the world can be viewed as such.

The story of a scholar from Fengyang in *Liaozhai Zhiyi* describes a strange dream that can be regarded as a cup of jealousy-curing soup. It and the play *The Secret of a Jealous Woman* performed by the famous actor Gou Huisheng can be said to have their own merits.

Jiang Yan's dream of flowers blooming from his brush has become a cliché of flattery for later generations. I don't know if Mr. Shao Yuanchong of the National Government also dreamed of a very thick brush that bloomed with flowers. He woke up feeling very surprised and ran to tell his wife, Ms. Zhang Mojun. Unexpectedly, Mojun also had the same dream. Later, when the Examination Yuan held its first examination, Yuanchong and Dai Jitao were appointed as chief examiners. To commemorate the auspicious dream, Yuanchong specially named his study "Hall of the Shared Dream of Flowers Blooming from the Brush." This can be regarded as a pleasant anecdote in the unofficial history of the party-state.

Lovers who have been separated for a long time are of course extremely happy when they dream of each other, but they are also very depressed when they wake up. I love the recent poem about dreams by Xi Jianhong and Lao Dan: "It is happy to meet in a dream, and the dream is also happy. It is not easy to meet, and it is difficult to dream of happiness. If you dream of meeting again, do not take it as a dream." It is said so thoroughly and lightly, truly an unsurpassed cooling agent for those in this situation.

Anecdotes from Nantong

— Wuxin

In the Yangtze River, less than dozens of *li* from Nantong, there is a "White Stomach Sand" that rises every day after sunset, like a sandbar, making it impossible for ships to move forward. Only after dawn, when the sand sinks down, can they continue to move forward. The timing of ships departing from Shanghai is always at 11 or 12 o'clock at night, precisely to avoid passing through this area at night. It is said that many domestic and foreign hydraulic experts have no solution to it. The wonders of the world are truly unexpected.

Mr. Zhang Jian did his best to support Mei Lanfang. Therefore, at the foot of Langshan Mountain, a scenic area in Nantong, he built a "Mei Residence" as a place for Mei to rest when he came to Nantong. In the past, this "Mei Residence" was about ten or twenty *li* away from the river, but now it is right next to the river. Therefore, it is expected that this "Mei Residence" will inevitably collapse into the river within a year or two. Many plum trees planted in front of the "Mei Residence" have already been moved away. Truly, the changes of time are rapid!

During the Ming Dynasty, Japanese pirates often invaded. In the thirty-sixth year of Jiajing, they even besieged Nantong with tens of thousands of troops. At that time, a man named Cao Ding led five hundred men and fought a bloody battle with the Japanese pirates, capturing many. However, in the end, he was killed due to the disparity in numbers. At this time of serious national crisis, in order to inspire the national spirit of the people, local people are building a Cao Gong Ancestral Hall.

Miracle

— Mei Jinghuo

I accidentally discovered this miracle in a remote tile and rubble field in Zhabei.

A cluster of twenty or thirty simple huts, viewed from a distance, looked like a pile of floating coffins in a field. Less than six feet high, a small hole about two feet wide was the only entrance and exit. The materials of these buildings (?) were entirely the broken walls and ruins of houses bombed by Japanese artillery fire during the Shanghai War, and a few pieces of rusted lead skin that had been abandoned by people.

When I stepped into this damp, dirty area, an unusual stench rushed into my olfactory organs. At the same time, several dove-shaped and stork-faced heads stretched out from the holes, looking at me with suspicious eyes deeply sunken in their sockets. In a flash, they shrank back. Encouraged by curiosity, I leaned down and peered into each hole, as if searching for a miracle. Ah! Could this be a red pill den? Each room had a broken mat, on which were placed small lamps, small boxes, and some scattered items. The users were mostly these ragged, disheveled beggars. Among them was even a female beggar of about twenty years old, who claimed that she had studied at a certain girls' school, but was expelled from her family for becoming addicted to red pills and ended up here. Indeed, she had a snake-like body and prominent hips, but she was not sensual. On her feet, she wore a pair of semi-new high-heeled shoes, like a modern woman, without socks. During the conversation, she even inserted a few sentences of accurately accented English. In my opinion, this cannot be said to be a miracle.

Ruyi Mulberry

— (Xia Hu)

It is said that Liu Bei of the Han Dynasty had a mulberry tree that stood tall like a child's umbrella, and the whole village regarded it as a treasure. The people of my hometown, Ganxiang, love to plant mulberry trees, but they only know how to pick the leaves to feed silkworms. They do not know that the branches and berries can also be used to treat diseases. Last summer, a mountain household named Hu from the North-South Lake area presented me with a Ruyi mulberry branch, which was quite peculiar, something I had never seen before. According to him: one evening, while enjoying the cool air in the courtyard, he caught a glimpse of a mulberry tree next to the house, which was emitting a strange light. The next morning, after examining the tree, he found a branch shaped like a Ruyi, flat, white, and covered with mulberry eyes, without a single leaf. He thought that such a strange mulberry branch was inauspicious, so he cut it off with scissors and casually put it into the rice basket. That night, the mulberry branch actually emitted a strange light, with the same brilliance as the night before. Moreover, from a distance, it looked like a mustache, wriggling. The light was emitted from this mustache. Upon closer inspection, he saw that there was indeed a mustache shape at the curved part. He was happy and played with it casually, but the mustache suddenly fell off, and from then on, it never emitted light again. An elderly neighbor over ninety years old said that this was called the Ruyi mulberry, and it should not be viewed too often, as it can cure all diseases.

— (Feng Sunmei's inscription)

Mr. Yang Wenqi from Minhou, also known as Shiquan Sanren, has a passion for collecting ancient coins and has a rich collection. It is now heard that Mr. Yang will donate more than two thousand ancient coins from his collection to the country for research. Once the new site of the Central Museum is completed, he will hand them over in full. The image above was taken during an exhibition at the Shanghai YMCA on New Year's Eve last year.

Small Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 10: Offending the Lady by Showing Off Wealth in Front of Her, Selecting a Wife by Coveting Her in the Shadows Due to Illness, One Loses Integrity

Yueying couldn't keep a straight face for long while Jia Duocai was admiring her, so she stood up and said: Mom! Can we go now? Madam Zhu Hu heard that Jia Duocai could give some money today, and her eyes were drawn to the pile of silver dollars on the corner of the table, constantly stealing glances at it. Because her eyes were drawn to the silver dollars, her body didn't want to leave, only hoping that Jia Duocai would grab a handful of silver coins and hand them over. However, Jia Duocai only said it but didn't act, and she herself was too embarrassed to leave, so she had to sit here and wait. Now that Yueying said she wanted to leave, she was unwilling to get up, so she said to her: What's the rush? There are still many things to talk about. Yueying raised her eyebrows and said: What else is there to talk about? I don't think it's appropriate for us to say it, and we can't say it well. Why don't you, auntie, say it? Madam Zhu Hu thought that she was too embarrassed to ask for money herself, so it would be good if her sister-in-law asked for it. So she supported herself on the chair and slowly stood up, saying to Jia Duocai: Master Jia, shall we go back? Jia Duocai smiled and took five silver dollars from the pile of silver dollars in his hand and handed them to Zhu Ming, placing them on the edge of the table. He smiled and said: You are honest people, and I can't deceive you. I'll give you this money first. It doesn't matter if things don't work out. I don't care. Madam Zhu Hu responded with "oh, oh" for a while, half-squatting and giving Jia Duocai an Anfu greeting with her hand on her chest. She smiled broadly, looked at him, and was about to thank him. Jia Duocai waved his hand and said: No need, no need. I only know today that your daughter can speak. Since she can speak, that's very good. I'll leave her here to sit for a while and have a heart-to-heart talk to see if she really wants to. There's nothing wrong with that, is there? Madam Zhu Hu felt that there was nothing wrong with it on the one hand, and on the other hand, she had received these five silver dollars, so she was too embarrassed to refuse. So she nodded and said: There's nothing important about that, but I'm afraid she'll be too embarrassed to say it, right? She then wanted to sit down again. (155)

Glimmers of Imperial Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Or it could be said that this was also a blessing for the Empress Dowager. Fortunately, Heaven did not grant her the ability to foresee the future. Otherwise, if she had known decades later that there would be a worthless thing like Puyi, who would be coerced by the Japanese into singing such a shameless opera in the three northeastern provinces, she would have died of anger long ago. In fact, at that time, Puyi was not even born yet, not to mention that the Empress Dowager would not have thought that he would be a Japanese puppet: even the title of Emperor of the puppet state for three years, she had not yet foreseen!

Upon entering the Summer Palace, all the historically sad flavors were cut off from her because this garden was newly built, and there were no sad memories left yet! And the various flowers that she loved were blooming in full bloom in the garden, which was enough to dispel all the sorrows in her heart. In addition, the gusts of warm breeze blowing down from the Western Hills swept through all parts of the garden, making people feel particularly comfortable and happy. That's right, this is her old home: and her retired resting place. In her twilight years, thanks to such a good place for her to enjoy herself, otherwise, the days she spent would have had no joy! What was most beneficial to her was that the garden was filled with three unique sights all year round: one was splendor, the second was tranquility, and the third was contentment. If she could see through everything and return all the power to Guangxu as before, her life would always have these three pleasant scenes: unfortunately, she could not, so she had to come to the garden on days when her political affairs were relatively leisurely to experience a moment of temporary tranquility and contentment. But when it came to splendor, it was all occupied by her: originally, what would be placed before the Empress Dowager's eyes would not be splendid? (266)

Local Customs

A Japanese Spectacle—Naked Shrine Festival

The "Naked Shrine Festival" is considered a wonder of the world by the Japanese. Examining its origins, it seems very similar to the "Beating Ghosts" custom in our country's Mongolian and Manchu customs, so it may have been passed down from ancient times in our country.

"Chasing away evil spirits" is the same as our country's "Beating Ghosts." It used to be a ritual performed in the Japanese court. "Da Nuo" refers to a big ghost, wearing a golden mask with four eyes on its head, dressed in black robes and a red skirt, holding a shield in its left hand and a dagger in its right. During the ceremony, after the Yin-Yang officials read the sacrificial text, they uttered the cries of small ghosts everywhere. Then the big ghost used the shield and dagger to drive the small ghosts out of the palace, praying for national peace and the happiness of the people. In spirit, after the evil ghosts are driven away, everyone's sins can be relieved.

This ritual has been passed down from ancient times to the present for over a thousand years. Now, shrines in various places have abolished it, but only the Guofu Yan Shrine still retains the ancient style. However, the rituals performed now are different from the form of "Chasing away evil spirits" in the palace in the past. The "Naked Festival" is held for a week, with the most grand event on the thirteenth day of the lunar new year. Society widely publicizes that in the past, the Japanese paid great attention to the Naked Festival. They all wore formal attire, fasted, bathed, and came from all directions to participate, hoping to eliminate their sins. Later, it gradually became casual, and the ceremony became very chaotic on the day of the festival. In the Tenmei period, the custom of nudity was a solemn divine affair. According to current regulations, men related to the evil spirits must strip naked and "rub shoulders" before they can eliminate their sins and prolong their lives.

According to old Japanese customs, the ages of twenty-five and forty-three are the years of misfortune. On the second day of the lunar new year, one must report to the shrine and select a "Year Man" by drawing lots. For the seven days before the "Inner Festival," one must stay in the Ghost Beating Hall for a fast. On the twelfth day of the lunar new year, the Shinto priests make a very large round New Year's cake with two or three liters of powder to worship the gods. On the morning of the thirteenth day, hundreds of naked men gather in the ritual field. At three o'clock in the afternoon, the Naked Festival begins. Everyone must go to the Ghost Beating Hall and rub the shoulders of the "Year Man" with their shoulders, and then rub each other's shoulders while circling in the hall. In this way, the skin heats up, and the water vapor rises, like a mist. More than ten thousand people come from near and far to watch the ceremony, and the fun is indescribable.

On the fourteenth day, the "Year Man" carries the large New Year's cake to the soil hill of "Little Mount Fuji" and digs a small hole to bury it. After chanting Buddhist scriptures for a few more days, the "Naked Festival" comes to an end. There is also a "Naked Festival" at the Kannon Hall of Saidaiji Temple in Bizen. More than one hundred thousand people come from the Keihan, Shikoku, and Kyushu regions. The rituals are slightly different and are held at 8 p.m. on the fourteenth day. Furthermore, at 2 a.m., the monks of Saidaiji Temple throw two wooden treasures from the window. The one who picks them up is called the "Lucky Man," and a group of naked men scramble for them.
